acerifolia">Platanus &#215; acerifolia</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[3]</a></sup></center><center><big><b>City flowers</b></big><br/> <a href="/wiki/Prunus_mume" title="Prunus mume">M&#233;i</a> (<i>Prunus mume</i>)</center></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr style="display:none;"><td colspan="2" style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Cantonese" title="Help:IPA/Cantonese">[na&#783;&#720;m.ke&#769;&#331;]</a></span></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a style="text-align:center;background-color: #dcffc9;"><a href="/wiki/Southern_Min" title="Southern Min">Southern Min</a></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Hokkien" System">T&#226;i-l&#244;</a></th><td><span lang="nan-Latn" style="font-style:normal" title="Taiwanese Hokkien-language transliteration">L&#226;m-kiann&#160;<small>(<a href="/wiki/Literary_and_colloquial_readings_of_Chinese_characters" title="Literary and colloquial readings of Chinese characters">col.</a>)</small><br/>L&#226;m-king&#160;<small>(<a href="/wiki/Literary_and_colloquial_readings_of_Chinese_characters" title="Literary and colloquial readings of Chinese characters">lit.</a>)</small></span></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Nanjing</b> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chinese-Nanjing.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/20/Zh-N%C3%A1nj%C4%ABng.oga" title="Zh-N&#225;nj&#299;ng.oga">listen</a></span></span>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Postal_Map_Romanization" title="Postal Map Romanization">formerly</a> <a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Chinese" title="Romanization of Chinese">romanized</a> as <b>Nanking</b> and <b>Nankin</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup> is the capital of <a href="/wiki/Jiangsu" title="Jiangsu">Jiangsu</a> province of the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People\'s Republic of China</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_China_by_population" title="List of cities in China by population">second largest city</a> in the <a href="/wiki/East_China" title="East China">East China</a> region,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[b]</a></sup> with an administrative area of 6,600&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (2,500&#160;sq&#160;mi) and a total population of 8,270,500 as of  2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[5]</a></sup> The inner area of Nanjing enclosed by <a href="/wiki/City_Wall_of_Nanjing" title="City Wall of Nanjing">the city wall</a> is Nanjing City (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#21335;&#20140;&#22478;</span>), with an area of 55&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (21&#160;sq&#160;mi), while the Nanjing Metropolitan Region includes surrounding cities and areas, covering over 60,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (23,000&#160;sq&#160;mi), with a population of over 30 million.\n</p><p>Situated in the <a href="/wiki/Yangtze_River_Delta" title="Yangtze River Delta">Yangtze River Delta</a> region, Nanjing has a prominent place in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_history" title="Chinese history">Chinese history</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_culture" title="Chinese culture">culture</a>, having served as the <a href="/wiki/Historical_capitals_of_China" title="Historical capitals of China">capital</a> of various Chinese dynasties, kingdoms and republican governments dating from the 3rd century to 1949,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-&#21382;&#21490;&#27839;&#38761;_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-&#21382;&#21490;&#27839;&#38761;-8">[6]</a></sup> and has thus long been a major center of culture, education, research, politics, economy, transport networks and tourism, being the home to <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Nanjing" title="Port of Nanjing">one of the world\'s largest inland ports</a>. The city is also one of the fifteen <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_city" title="Sub-provincial city">sub-provincial cities</a> in the People\'s Republic of China\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Administrative divisions of the People\'s Republic of China">administrative structure</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[7]</a></sup> enjoying jurisdictional and economic autonomy only slightly less than that of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Province_of_China" title="Province of China">province</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[8]</a></sup> Nanjing has been ranked seventh in the evaluation of "Cities with Strongest Comprehensive Strength" issued by the <a href="/wiki/National_Bureau_of_Statistics_of_China" title="National Bureau of Statistics of China">National Statistics Bureau</a>, and second in the evaluation of cities with most sustainable development potential in the Yangtze River Delta. It has also been awarded the title of 2008 Habitat Scroll of Honor of China, Special <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Habitat_Scroll_of_Honor_Award" title="UN Habitat Scroll of Honor Award">UN Habitat Scroll of Honor Award</a> and National Civilized City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[9]</a></sup> Nanjing boasts many high-quality universities and research institutes, with the number of universities listed in 100 National Key Universities ranking third, including <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_University" title="Nanjing University">Nanjing University</a> which has a long history and is among the world top 10 universities ranked by Nature Index.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup> The ratio of college students to total population ranks No.1 among large cities nationwide. Nanjing is one of the top three Chinese scientific research centers, according to the Nature Index,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[11]</a></sup> especially strong in the chemical sciences.\n</p><p>Nanjing, one of the nation\'s most important cities for over a thousand years, is recognized as one of the <a href="/wiki/Historical_capitals_of_China" title="Historical capitals of China">Four Great Ancient Capitals of China</a>. It has been one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities_throughout_history" title="List of largest cities throughout history">world\'s largest cities</a>, enjoying peace and prosperity despite wars and disasters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xinhua01_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-xinhua01-15">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-questia.com_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-questia.com-17">[15]</a></sup> Nanjing served as the capital of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Wu" title="Eastern Wu">Eastern Wu</a> (229&#8211;280), one of the three major states in the <a href="/wiki/Three_Kingdoms" title="Three Kingdoms">Three Kingdoms</a> period; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Jin_dynasty" title="Eastern Jin dynasty">Eastern Jin</a> and each of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_and_Northern_dynasties" title="Southern and Northern dynasties">Southern dynasties</a> (<a href="/wiki/Liu_Song_dynasty" title="Liu Song dynasty">Liu Song</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Qi" title="Southern Qi">Southern Qi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liang_dynasty" title="Liang dynasty">Liang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chen_dynasty" title="Chen dynasty">Chen</a>), which successively ruled southern China from 317&#8211;589; the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Tang" title="Southern Tang">Southern Tang</a> (937&#8211;75), one of the <a href="/wiki/Ten_Kingdoms" title="Ten Kingdoms">Ten Kingdoms</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> when, for the first time, all of China was ruled from the city (1368&#8211;1421);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crespigny_2004_loc=3_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Crespigny_2004_loc=3-18">[16]</a></sup> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%9349)" title="Republic of China (1912&#8211;49)">Republic of China</a> (1927&#8211;37, 1946&#8211;49) prior to its flight to <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Taiwan" title="Geography of Taiwan">Taiwan</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-capital-nanking_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-capital-nanking-19">[17]</a></sup> The city also served as the seat of the rebel <a href="/wiki/Taiping_Heavenly_Kingdom" title="Taiping Heavenly Kingdom">Taiping Heavenly Kingdom</a> (1853&#8211;64) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reorganized_National_Government_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="Reorganized National Government of the Republic of China">Japanese puppet regime of Wang Jingwei</a> (1940&#8211;45) during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a>. It suffered severe atrocities in both conflicts, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanking_Massacre" title="Nanking Massacre">Nanjing Massacre</a>.\n</p><p>Nanjing has served as the capital city of Jiangsu province since the establishment of the People\'s Republic of China. It boasts many important heritage sites, including the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Palace_(Nanjing)" title="Presidential Palace (Nanjing)">Presidential Palace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen_Mausoleum" title="Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum">Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum</a>. Nanjing is famous for human historical landscapes, mountains and waters such as <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Fuzimiao" title="Nanjing Fuzimiao">Fuzimiao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ming_Palace" title="Ming Palace">Ming Palace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chaotian_Palace" title="Chaotian Palace">Chaotian Palace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porcelain_Tower_of_Nanjing" title="Porcelain Tower of Nanjing">Porcelain Tower</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drum_Tower_of_Nanjing" title="Drum Tower of Nanjing">Drum Tower</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stone_City" title="Stone City">Stone City</a>, <a href="/wiki/City_Wall_of_Nanjing" title="City Wall of Nanjing">City Wall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qinhuai_River" title="Qinhuai River">Qinhuai River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xuanwu_Lake" title="Xuanwu Lake">Xuanwu Lake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Purple_Mountain_(Nanjing)" title="Purple Mountain (Nanjing)">Purple Mountain</a>. Key cultural facilities include <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Library" title="Nanjing Library">Nanjing Library</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Museum" title="Nanjing Museum">Nanjing Museum</a> and Nanjing Art Museum.\n</p><p><span id="Name"></span><span id="Etymology"></span><span id="Toponymy"></span>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" class="tocnumber">10.2</span> <span class="toctext">Parks and gardens</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40"><a href="#Other_places_of_interest"><span class="tocnumber">10.3</span> <span class="toctext">Other places of interest</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-42"><a href="#Universities_and_colleges"><span class="tocnumber">11.1</span> <span class="toctext">Universities and colleges</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-43"><a href="#Notable_high_schools"><span class="tocnumber">11.2</span> <span class="toctext">Notable high schools</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44"><a href="#Sister_cities"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Sister cities</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45"><a href="#Notable_people"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Notable people</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-47"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-48"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-49"><a href="#Citations"><span class="tocnumber">16.1</span> <span class="toctext">Citations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-50"><a href="#Sources"><span class="tocnumber">16.2</span> <span class="toctext">Sources</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-51"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Names">Names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The city has a number of other names, and some historical names are now used as names of districts of the city; among them there is the name <b>Jiangning</b> or <b>Kiangning</b> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">&#27743;&#23527;</span>), whose former character Jiang (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%B1%9F" title="wikt:&#27743;">&#27743;</a></span>, Yangtze) is the former part of the name <a href="/wiki/Jiangsu" title="Jiangsu">Jiangsu</a> and latter character <b>Ning</b> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%AF%A7" title="wikt:&#23527;">&#23527;</a></span>, simplified form <span lang="zh-Hans">&#23425;</span>; "Peace") is the short name of Nanjing. When it was the capital of a state, for instance during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%9349)" title="Republic of China (1912&#8211;49)">ROC</a>, Jing (<span lang="zh"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E4%BA%AC" title="wikt:&#20140;">&#20140;</a></span>; "Capital") was adopted as the abbreviation of Nanjing.\n</p><p>The city first became a Chinese national capital as early as the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(265%E2%80%93420)" title="Jin dynasty (265&#8211;420)">Jin dynasty</a>. The name <b>Nanjing</b>, which means "Southern Capital" (from the Chinese characters <span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%8D%97" title="wikt:&#21335;">&#21335;</a></span> for south and <span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#20140;</span> for capital), was officially designated for the city during the <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a>, about six hundred years later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[c]</a></sup> Nanjing is particularly known as <b>Jinling</b> or <b>Ginling</b> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#37329;&#38517;</span>, "Gold Hill") and the old name has been used since the <a href="/wiki/Warring_States_period" title="Warring States period">Warring States period</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Zhou_dynasty" title="Zhou dynasty">Zhou dynasty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[18]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Nanjing_history" title="Timeline of Nanjing history">Timeline of Nanjing history</a></div>\n<div //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a> <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="History of the People\'s Republic of China">People\'s Republic of China</a>, 1949&#8211;present<br/></div>\n</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Archaeological discovery shows that "<a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Man" title="Nanjing Man">Nanjing Man</a>" lived in more than 500 thousand years ago. <a href="/wiki/Zun" title="Zun">Zun</a>, a kind of wine vessel, was found to exist in Beiyinyangying culture of Nanjing in about 5000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[19]</a></sup> In the late period of <a href="/wiki/Shang_dynasty" title="Shang dynasty">Shang dynasty</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taibo_of_Wu" title="Taibo of Wu">Taibo</a> of <a href="/wiki/Predynastic_Zhou" title="Predynastic Zhou">Zhou</a> came to <a href="/wiki/Jiangnan" title="Jiangnan">Jiangnan</a> and established Wu state, and the first stop is in Nanjing area according to some historians based on discoveries in Taowu and Hushu culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[20]</a></sup> According to a legend quoted by an artist in Ming dynasty, Chen Yi, <a href="/wiki/Fuchai" title="Fuchai">Fuchai</a>, King of the <a href="/wiki/Wu_(state)" title="Wu (state)">State of Wu</a>, founded a fort named Yecheng in today\'s Nanjing area in 495<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[21]</a></sup> Later in 473<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Yue" title="State of Yue">State of Yue</a> conquered Wu and constructed the fort of <b>Yuecheng</b> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E8%B6%8A%E5%9F%8E" title="wikt:&#36234;&#22478;">&#36234;&#22478;</a></span>) on the outskirts of the present-day <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zhonghua_Gate" title="Zhonghua Gate">Zhonghua Gate</a>. In 333<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>, after eliminating the State of Yue, the <a href="/wiki/Chu_(state)" title="Chu (state)">State of Chu</a> built <b>Jinling Yi</b> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E9%87%91%E9%99%B5" title="wikt:&#37329;&#38517;">&#37329;&#38517;</a><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E9%82%91" title="wikt:&#37009;">&#37009;</a></span>) in the western part of present-day Nanjing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[22]</a></sup> It was renamed Moling (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E7%A7%A3%E9%99%B5" title="wikt:&#31203;&#38517;">&#31203;&#38517;</a></span>) during reign of <a href="/wiki/Qin_Shi_Huang" title="Qin Shi Huang">Qin Shi Huang</a>. Since then, the city experienced destruction and renewal many times.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The area was successively part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kuaiji_Prefecture" title="Kuaiji Prefecture">Kuaiji</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Zhang_Prefecture&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Zhang Prefecture (page does not exist)">Zhang</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Danyang_Prefecture&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Danyang Prefecture (page does not exist)">Danyang</a> prefectures in Qin and Han dynasty, and part of Yangzhou region which was established as the nation\'s 13 supervisory and administrative regions in the 5th year of Yuanfeng in Han dynasty (106<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>). Nanjing was later the capital city of Danyang Prefecture, and had been the capital city of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangzhou_(ancient_China)" title="Yangzhou (ancient China)">Yangzhou</a> for about 400 years from late <a href="/wiki/Han_dynasty" title="Han dynasty">Han</a> to early <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_China">Imperial China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Imperial China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Segalen-27-Xiao-Xiu-Winged-lion-right.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="303" data-file-width="401" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Segalen-27-Xiao-Xiu-Winged-lion-right.jpg/220px-Segalen-27-Xiao-Xiu-Winged-lion-right.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Segalen-27-Xiao-Xiu-Winged-lion-right.jpg/330px-Segalen-27-Xiao-Xiu-Winged-lion-right.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f2/Segalen-27-Xiao-Xiu-Winged-lion-right.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Segalen-27-Xiao-Xiu-Winged-lion-right.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bixie" title="Bixie">bixie</a></i> sculpture at <a href="/wiki/Xiao_Xiu" title="Xiao Xiu">Xiao Xiu</a>\'s tomb (<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">AD</span></span><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>518). <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stone_sculptures_at_mausoleum_of_the_southern_dynasties_in_Nanjing" title="Stone sculptures at mausoleum of the southern dynasties in Nanjing">Stone sculpture of the southern dynasties</a> is widely considered as the city\'s icon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[23]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Yuan_Dynasty_map_of_Nanjing,by_Chen_Yi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="444" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/The_Yuan_Dynasty_map_of_Nanjing%2Cby_Chen_Yi.jpg/220px-The_Yuan_Dynasty_map_of_Nanjing%2Cby_Chen_Yi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/The_Yuan_Dynasty_map_of_Nanjing%2Cby_Chen_Yi.jpg/330px-The_Yuan_Dynasty_map_of_Nanjing%2Cby_Chen_Yi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/The_Yuan_Dynasty_map_of_Nanjing%2Cby_Chen_Yi.jpg/440px-The_Yuan_Dynasty_map_of_Nanjing%2Cby_Chen_Yi.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Yuan_Dynasty_map_of_Nanjing,by_Chen_Yi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Yuan dynasty map of Nanjing.</div></div></div>\n<p>Nanjing first became a state capital in <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">AD</span></span><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>229, when the state of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Wu" title="Eastern Wu">Eastern Wu</a> founded by <a href="/wiki/Sun_Quan" title="Sun Quan">Sun Quan</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Three_Kingdoms" title="Three Kingdoms">Three Kingdoms</a> period relocated its capital to <b><a href="/wiki/Jianye_District" title="Jianye District">Jianye</a></b> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%BB%BA%E6%A5%AD" title="wikt:&#24314;&#26989;">&#24314;&#26989;</a></span>), the city extended on the basis of Jinling Yi in <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">AD</span></span><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>211.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crespigny_2004_loc=3_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Crespigny_2004_loc=3-18">[16]</a></sup> Although conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(265%E2%80%93420)" title="Jin dynasty (265&#8211;420)">Western Jin dynasty</a> in 280, Nanjing and its neighboring areas had been well cultivated and developed into one of the commercial, cultural and political centers of China during the rule of East Wu.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-questia.com_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-questia.com-17">[15]</a></sup> This city would soon play a vital role in the following centuries.\n</p><p>Shortly after the unification of the region, the Western Jin dynasty collapsed. First the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Eight_Princes" title="War of the Eight Princes">rebellions by eight Jin princes</a> for the throne and later rebellions and invasion from <a href="/wiki/Xiongnu" title="Xiongnu">Xiongnu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Five_Barbarians" title="Five Barbarians">other nomadic peoples</a> that destroyed the rule of the Jin dynasty in the north. In 317, remnants of the Jin court, as well as nobles and wealthy families, fled from the north to the south and reestablished the Jin court in Nanjing, which was then called <b><a href="/wiki/Jiankang" title="Jiankang">Jiankang</a></b> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%BB%BA%E5%BA%B7" title="wikt:&#24314;&#24247;">&#24314;&#24247;</a></span>), replacing <a href="/wiki/Luoyang" title="Luoyang">Luoyang</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liu_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-liu-27">[24]</a></sup> This marked the first time a Chinese dynastic capital moved to <a href="/wiki/Northern_and_southern_China" title="Northern and southern China">southern China</a>.\n</p><p>During the period of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_and_Northern_Dynasties" title="Southern and Northern Dynasties">North&#8211;South division</a>, Nanjing remained the capital of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_dynasties" title="Southern dynasties">Southern dynasties</a> for more than two and a half centuries. During this time, Nanjing was the international hub of East Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[25]</a></sup> Based on historical documents, the city had 280,000 registered households.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[26]</a></sup> Assuming an average Nanjing household consisted of about 5.1 people, the city had more than 1.4&#160;million residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liu_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-liu-27">[24]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A number of <a href="/wiki/Spirit_way" title="Spirit way">sculptural ensembles</a> of that era, erected at the tombs of royals and other dignitaries, have survived (in various degrees of preservation) in Nanjing\'s northeastern and eastern suburbs, primarily in <a href="/wiki/Qixia_District" title="Qixia District">Qixia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jiangning_District" title="Jiangning District">Jiangning District</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[27]</a></sup> Possibly the best preserved of them is the ensemble of the Tomb of <a href="/wiki/Xiao_Xiu" title="Xiao Xiu">Xiao Xiu</a> (475&#8211;518), a brother of <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Wu_of_Liang" title="Emperor Wu of Liang">Emperor Wu of Liang</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[29]</a></sup> The period of division ended when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sui_Dynasty" title="Sui Dynasty">Sui Dynasty</a> reunified China and almost destroyed the entire city, turning it into a small town.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nanjing_in_Ming_Dynasty.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="767" data-file-width="1086" decoding="async" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Nanjing_in_Ming_Dynasty.jpg/320px-Nanjing_in_Ming_Dynasty.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Nanjing_in_Ming_Dynasty.jpg/480px-Nanjing_in_Ming_Dynasty.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Nanjing_in_Ming_Dynasty.jpg/640px-Nanjing_in_Ming_Dynasty.jpg 2x" width="320"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nanjing_in_Ming_Dynasty.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Yingtian Fu under the Ming</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pagoda_at_Qixia_Temple_Nanjing.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1524" data-file-width="1016" decoding="async" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Pagoda_at_Qixia_Temple_Nanjing.jpg/220px-Pagoda_at_Qixia_Temple_Nanjing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Pagoda_at_Qixia_Temple_Nanjing.jpg/330px-Pagoda_at_Qixia_Temple_Nanjing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Pagoda_at_Qixia_Temple_Nanjing.jpg/440px-Pagoda_at_Qixia_Temple_Nanjing.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pagoda_at_Qixia_Temple_Nanjing.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Aar%C4%ABra" title="&#346;ar&#299;ra">&#346;ar&#299;ra</a> <a href="/wiki/Pagoda" title="Pagoda">pagoda</a> in <a href="/wiki/Qixia_Temple" title="Qixia Temple">Qixia Temple</a>. It was built in <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">AD</span></span><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>601 and rebuilt in the 10th century.</div></div></div>\n<p>The city of Nanjing was razed after the <a href="/wiki/Sui_dynasty" title="Sui dynasty">Sui dynasty</a> took it over.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[30]</a></sup> It was renamed Shengzhou (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#26119;&#24030;</span>) in the <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang dynasty</a> and resuscitated during the late Tang.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[31]</a></sup> It was chosen as the capital and called <b>Jinling</b> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E9%87%91%E9%99%B5" title="wikt:&#37329;&#38517;">&#37329;&#38517;</a></span>) during the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Tang" title="Southern Tang">Southern Tang</a> (937&#8211;976), a state that succeeded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wu_(Ten_Kingdoms)" title="Wu (Ten Kingdoms)">Wu state</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[32]</a></sup> It was renamed Jiangning (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%B1%9F%E5%AF%A7" title="wikt:&#27743;&#23527;">&#27743;&#23527;</a></span>) in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Song_dynasty" title="Northern Song dynasty">Northern Song dynasty</a> and renamed Jiankang in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Song_dynasty" title="Southern Song dynasty">Southern Song dynasty</a>. Jiankang\'s textile industry burgeoned and thrived during the <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasty</a> despite the constant threat of foreign <a href="/wiki/Jin%E2%80%93Song_Wars" title="Jin&#8211;Song Wars">invasions from the north</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Jurchen_people" title="Jurchen people">Jurchen</a>-led <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115&#8211;1234)">Jin dynasty</a>. The court of <a href="/wiki/Da_Chu" title="Da Chu">Da Chu</a>, a short-lived puppet state established by the Jurchens, and the court of Song were once in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[35]</a></sup> Song was eventually exterminated by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_empire" title="Mongol empire">Mongol empire</a> under the name <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan</a> and in the Yuan dynasty the city\'s status as a hub of the textile industry was further consolidated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[36]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B3-%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B3-%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0.JPG/220px-%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B3-%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B3-%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0.JPG/330px-%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B3-%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B3-%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0.JPG/440px-%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B3-%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B3-%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gate_of_China,_Nanjing" title="Gate of China, Nanjing">Zhonghua Gate</a> is the south gate of the walled city of Nanjing. The <a href="/wiki/City_Wall_of_Nanjing" title="City Wall of Nanjing">city wall</a> was built in the 14th century and is the longest in the world.</div></div></div>\n<p>The first emperor of the <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a>, Zhu Yuanzhang (the <a href="/wiki/Hongwu_Emperor" title="Hongwu Emperor">Hongwu Emperor</a>), who overthrew the Yuan dynasty, renamed the city <b>Yingtian</b>, rebuilt it, and made it the dynastic capital in 1368. He constructed a 48&#160;km (30&#160;mi) long <a href="/wiki/City_Wall_of_Nanjing" title="City Wall of Nanjing">city wall around Yingtian</a>, as well as a new <a href="/wiki/Ming_Palace" title="Ming Palace">Ming Palace</a> complex, and government halls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ebrey_cambridge_191_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-ebrey_cambridge_191-40">[37]</a></sup> It took 200,000 laborers 21&#160;years to finish the project. The present-day <a href="/wiki/City_Wall_of_Nanjing" title="City Wall of Nanjing">City Wall of Nanjing</a> was mainly built during that time and today it remains in good condition and has been well preserved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[38]</a></sup> It is among the longest surviving <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_wall" title="City wall">city walls</a> in China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[39]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Jianwen_Emperor" title="Jianwen Emperor">Jianwen Emperor</a> ruled from 1398 to 1402.\n</p><p>It is believed that Nanjing was the largest city in the world from 1358 to 1425 with a population of 487,000 in 1400.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[40]</a></sup> In 1421, the Yongle Emperor persisted in relocating the capital to Beijing, however he had to withdraw his order before his death. His successor, the <a href="/wiki/Hongxi_Emperor" title="Hongxi Emperor">Hongxi Emperor</a>, wished to revert the relocation of the imperial capital from Nanjing to Beijing that had happened during the Yongle reign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dr7-13940_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-dr7-13940-44">[41]</a></sup> On 24 February 1425, he appointed Admiral <a href="/wiki/Zheng_He" title="Zheng He">Zheng He</a> as the defender of Nanjing and ordered him to continue his command over the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ming_treasure_fleet" title="Ming treasure fleet">Ming treasure fleet</a> for the city\'s defenses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dr7-13940_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-dr7-13940-44">[41]</a></sup> Zheng He governed the city with three eunuchs for internal matters and two military noblemen for external matters, awaiting the Hongxi Emperor\'s return along with the military establishment from the north.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dr7-13940_44-2"><a href="#cite_note-dr7-13940-44">[41]</a></sup> The emperor died on 29 May 1425 before this could have taken place,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dr7-13940_44-3"><a href="#cite_note-dr7-13940-44">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ch98-282-3_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-ch98-282-3-45">[42]</a></sup> so Beijing remained the <i>de facto</i> capital and Nanjing remained the secondary capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ch98-282-3_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-ch98-282-3-45">[42]</a></sup> The succeeding <a href="/wiki/Xuande_Emperor" title="Xuande Emperor">Xuande Emperor</a> remained in Beijing, so the aforementioned Nanjing government eventually became a permanent institution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[43]</a></sup> In official Ming documents of 1425 to 1441, Nanjing was designated as the capital and Beijing was designated as the temporary capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[44]</a></sup> In 1441, <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Jingzong_of_Tang" title="Emperor Jingzong of Tang">Emperor Yingzong</a> ordered to not to prefix the word "provisional" (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E8%A1%8C" title="wikt:&#34892;">&#34892;</a><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%9C%A8" title="wikt:&#22312;">&#22312;</a></span>) on the Beijing Government seals any longer, while Nanjing\'s need to prefix "Nanjing" for distinguishing purposes remained. Hence, Nanjing still had itself imperial government with extremely limit power before 1644.\n</p><p>Besides the city wall, other famous Ming-era structures in the city included the famous <a href="/wiki/Ming_Xiaoling_Mausoleum" title="Ming Xiaoling Mausoleum">Ming Xiaoling Mausoleum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Porcelain_Tower_of_Nanjing" title="Porcelain Tower of Nanjing">Porcelain Tower</a>, although the latter was destroyed by the <a href="/wiki/Taiping_Rebellion" title="Taiping Rebellion">Taipings</a> in the 19th century either in order to prevent a hostile faction from using it to observe and shell the city<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[45]</a></sup> or from superstitious fear of its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fengshui" title="Fengshui">geomantic properties</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[46]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A monument to the huge human cost of some of the gigantic construction projects of the early Ming dynasty is the <a href="/wiki/Yangshan_Quarry" title="Yangshan Quarry">Yangshan Quarry</a> (located some 15&#8211;20&#160;km (9&#8211;12&#160;mi) east of the walled city and Ming Xiaoling mausoleum), where a gigantic <a href="/wiki/Stele" title="Stele">stele</a>, cut on the orders of the Yongle Emperor, lies abandoned, just as it was left 600&#160;years ago when it was understood it was impossible to move or complete it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-njmq_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-njmq-50">[47]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Du_Halde,_map_of_Nanjing.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1150" data-file-width="1036" decoding="async" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Du_Halde%2C_map_of_Nanjing.jpg/200px-Du_Halde%2C_map_of_Nanjing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Du_Halde%2C_map_of_Nanjing.jpg/300px-Du_Halde%2C_map_of_Nanjing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Du_Halde%2C_map_of_Nanjing.jpg/400px-Du_Halde%2C_map_of_Nanjing.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Du_Halde,_map_of_Nanjing.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Du_Halde" title="Du Halde">Du Halde</a>\'s 1736 map of "Nan-king", based on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit_China_mission" title="Jesuit China mission">Jesuit</a> accounts</div></div></div>\n<p>As the center of the empire, early-Ming Nanjing had worldwide connections. It was home of the admiral <a href="/wiki/Zheng_He" title="Zheng He">Zheng He</a>, who went to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treasure_voyages" title="Treasure voyages">sail the Pacific and Indian Oceans</a>, and it was visited by foreign dignitaries, such as a king from Borneo (<span lang="zh">&#28196;&#27877;</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">B&#243;n&#237;</span></i>), who died during his visit to China in 1408. The <a href="/wiki/Tomb_of_the_King_of_Boni" title="Tomb of the King of Boni">Tomb of the King of Boni</a>, with a spirit way and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bixi_(tortoise)" title="Bixi (tortoise)">tortoise stele</a>, was discovered in <a href="/wiki/Yuhuatai_District" title="Yuhuatai District">Yuhuatai District</a> (south of the walled city) in 1958, and has been restored.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[48]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Over two centuries after the removal of the capital to Beijing, Nanjing was destined to become the capital of a Ming emperor one more time. After the fall of Beijing to <a href="/wiki/Li_Zicheng" title="Li Zicheng">Li Zicheng</a>\'s rebel forces and then to the <a href="/wiki/Manchu_people" title="Manchu people">Manchu</a>-led <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing dynasty</a> in the spring of 1644, the Ming prince <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zhu_Yousong,_Prince_of_Fu" title="Zhu Yousong, Prince of Fu">Zhu Yousong</a> was enthroned in Nanjing in June 1644 as the Hongguang Emperor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wakeman_346_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wakeman_346-52">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup> His short reign was described by later historians as the first reign of the so-called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Ming_dynasty" title="Southern Ming dynasty">Southern Ming dynasty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[51]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Zhu Yousong, however, fared a lot worse than his ancestor Zhu Yuanzhang three centuries earlier. Beset by factional conflicts, his regime could not offer effective resistance to Qing forces, when the Qing army, led by the Manchu prince <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dodo_(prince)" title="Dodo (prince)">Dodo</a> approached <a href="/wiki/Jiangnan" title="Jiangnan">Jiangnan</a> the next spring.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup> Days after <a href="/wiki/Yangzhou" title="Yangzhou">Yangzhou</a> fell to the Manchus in late May 1645, the Hongguang Emperor fled Nanjing, and the imperial Ming Palace was looted by local residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[53]</a></sup> On June 6, Dodo\'s troops approached Nanjing, and the commander of the city\'s garrison, Zhao the Earl of Xincheng, promptly surrendered the city to them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[55]</a></sup> The Manchus soon ordered all male residents of the city to shave their heads in the <a href="/wiki/Queue_(hairstyle)" title="Queue (hairstyle)">Manchu queue way</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[56]</a></sup> They requisitioned a large section of the city for the <a href="/wiki/Eight_Banners" title="Eight Banners">bannermen</a>\'s cantonment, and destroyed the former imperial <a href="/wiki/Ming_Palace" title="Ming Palace">Ming Palace</a>, but otherwise the city was spared the mass murders and destruction that <a href="/wiki/Yangzhou_massacre" title="Yangzhou massacre">befell Yangzhou</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[57]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Regaining_Jinling.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1361" data-file-width="2343" decoding="async" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Regaining_Jinling.jpg/200px-Regaining_Jinling.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Regaining_Jinling.jpg/300px-Regaining_Jinling.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Regaining_Jinling.jpg/400px-Regaining_Jinling.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Regaining_Jinling.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An artist\'s impression of the <a href="/wiki/Taiping_Rebellion" title="Taiping Rebellion">Taiping Rebellion</a> (1850&#8211;1864).</div></div></div>\n<p>Under the <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing dynasty</a> (1644&#8211;1911), the Nanjing area was known as <b>Jiangning</b> and served as the seat of government for the <a href="/wiki/Viceroy_of_Liangjiang" title="Viceroy of Liangjiang">Viceroy of Liangjiang</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[58]</a></sup> It was the site of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qing_Army" title="Qing Army">Qing army</a> garrison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[59]</a></sup> It had been visited by the <a href="/wiki/Kangxi_Emperor" title="Kangxi Emperor">Kangxi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qianlong_Emperor" title="Qianlong Emperor">Qianlong</a> emperors a number of times on their tours of the southern provinces. Nanjing was threatened to be invaded by British troops during the close of the <a href="/wiki/First_Opium_War" title="First Opium War">First Opium War</a>, which was ended by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nanking" title="Treaty of Nanking">Treaty of Nanjing</a> in 1842. As the capital of the brief-lived rebel <a href="/wiki/Taiping_Heavenly_Kingdom" title="Taiping Heavenly Kingdom">Taiping Heavenly Kingdom</a> (founded by the <a href="/wiki/Taiping_Rebellion" title="Taiping Rebellion">Taiping rebels</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[60]</a></sup> in the mid-19th century, Nanjing was known as <b>Tianjing</b> (<span lang="zh"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%A4%A9" title="wikt:&#22825;">&#22825;</a><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E4%BA%AC" title="wikt:&#20140;">&#20140;</a></span>; ""Heavenly Capital" or "Capital of Heaven"").\n</p><p>Both the Qing viceroy and the Taiping king resided in buildings that would later be known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidential_Building_(Nanjing)" title="Presidential Building (Nanjing)">Presidential Palace</a>. When Qing forces led by <a href="/wiki/Zeng_Guofan" title="Zeng Guofan">Zeng Guofan</a> retook the city in 1864, a massive slaughter occurred in the city with over 100,000 estimated to have committed suicide or fought to the death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[61]</a></sup> Since the Taiping Rebellion began, Qing forces allowed no rebels speaking its dialect to surrender.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[62]</a></sup> This systematic mass murder of civilians occurred in Nanjing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[63]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Statue1_of_Qianfoya_Nanjing.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1524" data-file-width="1016" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Statue1_of_Qianfoya_Nanjing.jpg/80px-Statue1_of_Qianfoya_Nanjing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Statue1_of_Qianfoya_Nanjing.jpg/120px-Statue1_of_Qianfoya_Nanjing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Statue1_of_Qianfoya_Nanjing.jpg/160px-Statue1_of_Qianfoya_Nanjing.jpg 2x" width="80"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Statue1 of Qianfoya Nanjing\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:34px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wenceslas_Hollar_-_Pagoda_of_Paolinx.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2569" data-file-width="3758" decoding="async" height="82" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Wenceslas_Hollar_-_Pagoda_of_Paolinx.jpg/180px-Wenceslas_Hollar_-_Pagoda_of_Paolinx.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Wenceslas_Hollar_-_Pagoda_of_Paolinx.jpg/240px-Wenceslas_Hollar_-_Pagoda_of_Paolinx.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Wenceslas Hollar - Pagoda of Paolinx\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:30px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nanjing_DonghuaGate4.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="90" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Nanjing_DonghuaGate4.jpg/180px-Nanjing_DonghuaGate4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Nanjing_DonghuaGate4.jpg/240px-Nanjing_DonghuaGate4.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Nanjing Donghua Gate\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:35px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:YiFeng_Gate_Nanjing.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1016" data-file-width="1524" decoding="async" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/YiFeng_Gate_Nanjing.jpg/120px-YiFeng_Gate_Nanjing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/YiFeng_Gate_Nanjing.jpg/180px-YiFeng_Gate_Nanjing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/YiFeng_Gate_Nanjing.jpg/240px-YiFeng_Gate_Nanjing.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>YiFeng Gate\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:30px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E6%98%8E%E5%AD%9D%E9%99%B5-%E5%A4%A7%E9%87%91%E9%97%A8.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="90" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/%E6%98%8E%E5%AD%9D%E9%99%B5-%E5%A4%A7%E9%87%91%E9%97%A8.jpg/120px-%E6%98%8E%E5%AD%9D%E9%99%B5-%E5%A4%A7%E9%87%91%E9%97%A8.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/%E6%98%8E%E5%AD%9D%E9%99%B5-%E5%A4%A7%E9%87%91%E9%97%A8.jpg/180px-%E6%98%8E%E5%AD%9D%E9%99%B5-%E5%A4%A7%E9%87%91%E9%97%A8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/%E6%98%8E%E5%AD%9D%E9%99%B5-%E5%A4%A7%E9%87%91%E9%97%A8.jpg/240px-%E6%98%8E%E5%AD%9D%E9%99%B5-%E5%A4%A7%E9%87%91%E9%97%A8.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Ming Xiaoling Mausoleum\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_China">Modern China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Modern China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><b>Religion/Medicine</b>\n</p><p>The New York Methodist Mission Society\'s Superintendent, Virgil Hart arrived in Nanking in 1881. After some time, he eventually thwarted its officials by buying a piece of property near the South Gate and Confucius Temple; to build the city\'s first Methodist Church, western hospital (Blackstone Methodist Hospital) and Boy\'s School. The hospital would later be unified with the Drum Tower Hospital and the Boy\'s School would be expanded by later Missionaries to become the University of Nanking and Medical School. The old Mission property would become the #13 Middle School, the city\'s oldest/continuous school grounds in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[64]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nanking" title="Battle of Nanking">Battle of Nanking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Massacre" title="Nanjing Massacre">Nanjing Massacre</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Xinhai_Revolution" title="Xinhai Revolution">Xinhai Revolution</a> led to the founding of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%9349)" title="Republic of China (1912&#8211;49)">Republic of China</a> in January 1912 with <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen" title="Sun Yat-sen">Sun Yat-sen</a> as the first provisional president and Nanking was selected as its new capital. However, the Qing Empire controlled large regions to the north, so revolutionaries asked <a href="/wiki/Yuan_Shikai" title="Yuan Shikai">Yuan Shikai</a> to replace Sun as president in exchange for the abdication of <a href="/wiki/Puyi" title="Puyi">Puyi</a>, the Last Emperor. Yuan demanded the capital be <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> (closer to his power base).\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:National_Government_of_the_R.O.C.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="884" data-file-width="1323" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/National_Government_of_the_R.O.C.jpg/220px-National_Government_of_the_R.O.C.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/National_Government_of_the_R.O.C.jpg/330px-National_Government_of_the_R.O.C.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/National_Government_of_the_R.O.C.jpg/440px-National_Government_of_the_R.O.C.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:National_Government_of_the_R.O.C.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The headquarters of the National Government of the Republic of China in Nanjing, 1927</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1927, the <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a> (KMT; Nationalist Party) under Generalissimo <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a> again established Nanjing as the capital of the Republic of China, and this became internationally recognized once KMT forces took Beijing in 1928. The following decade is known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanking_decade" title="Nanking decade">Nanking decade</a>.\n</p><p>In 1937, the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a> started a full-scale invasion of China after invading Manchuria in 1931, beginning the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a> (often considered a theater of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[65]</a></sup> Their troops occupied Nanjing in December and carried out the systematic and brutal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanking_Massacre" title="Nanking Massacre">Nanking Massacre</a> (the "Rape of Nanking").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-69">[66]</a></sup> Even children, the elderly, and nuns are reported to have suffered at the hands of the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army" title="Imperial Japanese Army">Imperial Japanese Army</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[67]</a></sup> The total death toll, including estimates made by the <a href="/wiki/International_Military_Tribunal_for_the_Far_East" title="International Military Tribunal for the Far East">International Military Tribunal for the Far East</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_War_Crimes_Tribunal" title="Nanjing War Crimes Tribunal">Nanjing War Crimes Tribunal</a> after the atomic bombings, was between 300,000 and 350,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[68]</a></sup> The city itself was also severely damaged during the massacre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-69">[66]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanjing_Massacre_Memorial_Hall" title="Nanjing Massacre Memorial Hall">Nanjing Massacre Memorial Hall</a> was built in 1985 to commemorate this event.\n</p><p>A few days before the fall of the city, the National Government of China was relocated to the southwestern city <a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">Chungking (Chongqing)</a> and resumed Chinese resistance. In 1940, a Japanese-collaborationist government known as the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wang_Jingwei_Government" title="Wang Jingwei Government">Nanjing Regime</a>" or "Reorganized National Government of China" led by <a href="/wiki/Wang_Jingwei" title="Wang Jingwei">Wang Jingwei</a> was established in Nanjing as a rival to <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a>\'s government in Chongqing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[69]</a></sup> In 1946, after the <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">Surrender of Japan</a>, the KMT relocated its central government back to Nanjing.\n</p><p>On 21 April 1949, Communist forces crossed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze River</a>. On April 23, the Communist <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People\'s Liberation Army">People\'s Liberation Army</a> (PLA) captured Nanjing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zhang_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zhang-73">[70]</a></sup> The KMT government retreated to Canton (<a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a>) until October 15, <a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">Chongqing</a> until November 25, and then <a href="/wiki/Chengdu" title="Chengdu">Chengdu</a> before retreating to the <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Taiwan" title="Geography of Taiwan">island of Taiwan</a> on December 10 where <a href="/wiki/Taipei" title="Taipei">Taipei</a> was proclaimed the <a href="/wiki/Temporary_capital" title="Temporary capital">temporary capital</a> of the Republic of China. By late 1949, the PLA was pursuing remnants of KMT forces southwards in southern China, and only <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tibet_(1912%E2%80%9351)" title="Tibet (1912&#8211;51)">Tibet</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hainan_Island" title="Hainan Island">Hainan Island</a> were left. After the establishment of the People\'s Republic of China in October 1949, Nanjing was initially a province-level municipality, but it was soon merged into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jiangsu_province" title="Jiangsu province">Jiangsu province</a> and again became the provincial capital by replacing <a href="/wiki/Zhenjiang" title="Zhenjiang">Zhenjiang</a> which was transferred in 1928, and retains that status to this day.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:52.5px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Signing_of_the_Treaty_of_Nanking.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3633" data-file-width="9686" decoding="async" height="45" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/The_Signing_of_the_Treaty_of_Nanking.jpg/120px-The_Signing_of_the_Treaty_of_Nanking.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/The_Signing_of_the_Treaty_of_Nanking.jpg/180px-The_Signing_of_the_Treaty_of_Nanking.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/The_Signing_of_the_Treaty_of_Nanking.jpg/240px-The_Signing_of_the_Treaty_of_Nanking.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>The Signing of the Treaty of Nanking&#65288;1842&#65289;\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n<div class="thumb" 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Nanking&#65288;1871&#65289;\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:30px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Former_Residence_of_Song_Ziwen_in_Nanjing_2011-03.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2990" width="120"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Former Residence of Song Ziwen in Nanjing\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: width="90"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Former Management Bureau of Jiangsu Postal Service\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nanjing_Area_-_Lower_Yangtse_Valley_%26_Eastern_China_Map.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="432" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Nanjing_Area_-_Lower_Yangtse_Valley_%26_Eastern_China_Map.jpg/220px-Nanjing_Area_-_Lower_Yangtse_Valley_%26_Eastern_China_Map.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Nanjing_Area_-_Lower_Yangtse_Valley_%26_Eastern_China_Map.jpg/330px-Nanjing_Area_-_Lower_Yangtse_Valley_%26_Eastern_China_Map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1d/Nanjing_Area_-_Lower_Yangtse_Valley_%26_Eastern_China_Map.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nanjing_Area_-_Lower_Yangtse_Valley_%26_Eastern_China_Map.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nanjing Region - Lower Yangtze Basin and Eastern China.</div></div></div>\n<p>Nanjing, with a total land area of 6,598&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (2,548&#160;sq&#160;mi), is situated in the heartland of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drainage_area" title="Drainage area">drainage area</a> of the lower reaches of the Yangtze River, and in the Yangtze River Delta, one of the largest economic zones of China. The Yangtze River flows past the west side and then the north side of Nanjing City, while the Ningzheng Ridge surrounds the north, east and south sides of the city. The city is 650&#160;km (400&#160;mi) southeast of <a href="/wiki/Luoyang" title="Luoyang">Luoyang</a>, 1,200&#160;km (750&#160;mi) south-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, 300&#160;km (190&#160;mi) west-northwest of <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>, and 1,400&#160;km (870&#160;mi) east-northeast of <a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">Chongqing</a>. The Yangtze River flows downstream from <a href="/wiki/Jiujiang" title="Jiujiang">Jiujiang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jiangxi" title="Jiangxi">Jiangxi</a>, through <a href="/wiki/Anhui" title="Anhui">Anhui</a> and Jiangsu to the East China Sea. The northern part of the lower Yangtze drainage basin is the <a href="/wiki/Huai_River" title="Huai River">Huai River</a> basin and the southern part is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zhe_River" title="Zhe River">Zhe River</a> basin; they are connected by the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Canal_(China)" title="Grand Canal (China)">Grand Canal</a> east of Nanjing. The area around Nanjing is called Xiajiang (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#19979;&#27743;</span>, Downstream River) region, with <a href="/wiki/Jianghuai" title="Jianghuai">Jianghuai</a> dominant in the northern part and <a href="/wiki/Wu_(region)" title="Wu (region)">Jiangzhe</a> dominant in the southern part.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[d]</a></sup> The region is also well known as Dongnan (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">&#26481;&#21335;</span>, South East, the Southeast) and <a href="/wiki/Jiangnan" title="Jiangnan">Jiangnan</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#27743;&#21335;</span>, and River South, South of Yangtze).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[e]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nanjing borders <a href="/wiki/Yangzhou" title="Yangzhou">Yangzhou</a> to the northeast (one town downstream when following the north bank of the Yangtze); <a href="/wiki/Zhenjiang" title="Zhenjiang">Zhenjiang</a> to the east (one town downstream when following the south bank of the Yangtze); and <a href="/wiki/Changzhou" title="Changzhou">Changzhou</a> to the southeast. On its western boundary is <a href="/wiki/Anhui" title="Anhui">Anhui</a> province, where Nanjing borders five prefecture-level cities: <a href="/wiki/Chuzhou" title="Chuzhou">Chuzhou</a> to the northwest, <a href="/wiki/Wuhu" title="Wuhu">Wuhu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chaohu" title="Chaohu">Chaohu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ma%27anshan" title="Ma\'anshan">Ma\'anshan</a> to the west and <a href="/wiki/Xuancheng" title="Xuancheng">Xuancheng</a> to the southwest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-&#24066;&#24535;_&#24066;&#22495;_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-&#24066;&#24535;_&#24066;&#22495;-76">[71]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nanjing is at the intersection of the Yangtze River, an east-west water transport artery, and the Nanjing&#8211;Beijing railway, a north-south land transport artery, hence the name &#8220;door of the east and west, throat of the south and north&#8221;. Furthermore, the west part of the Ningzhen range is in Nanjing; the Loong-like Zhong Mountain curls round the east side of the city, while the tiger-like Stone Mountain crouches in the west of the city, hence the name &#8220;the Zhong Mountain, a dragon curling, and the Stone Mountain, a tiger crouching&#8221;.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_and_environment">Climate and environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Climate and environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="infobox" style="width: 19.5em; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: red">Average max. and min. temperatures in &#176;F</td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: blue">Precipitation totals in inches</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Qixia_Mountain_Autumn.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2368" data-file-width="4208" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Qixia_Mountain_Autumn.jpg/220px-Qixia_Mountain_Autumn.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Qixia_Mountain_Autumn.jpg/330px-Qixia_Mountain_Autumn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Qixia_Mountain_Autumn.jpg/440px-Qixia_Mountain_Autumn.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Qixia_Mountain_Autumn.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Autumn maple leaves in <a href="/wiki/Qixia_Mountain" title="Qixia Mountain">Qixia Mountain Temple</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Nanjing has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification">K&#246;ppen</a> <i>Cfa</i>) and is under the influence of the East Asian <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a>. The four seasons are distinct, with damp conditions seen throughout the year, very hot and muggy summers, cold, damp winters, and in between, spring and autumn are of reasonable length. Along with <a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">Chongqing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wuhan" title="Wuhan">Wuhan</a>, Nanjing is traditionally referred to as one of the "<a href="/wiki/Three_Furnaces" title="Three Furnaces">Three Furnacelike Cities</a>" along the Yangtze River for the perennially high temperatures in the summertime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[73]</a></sup> However, the time from mid-June to the end of July is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plum_blossom" title="Plum blossom">plum blossom</a> blooming season in which the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meiyu" title="Meiyu">meiyu</a></i> (rainy season of East Asia; literally "plum rain") occurs, during which the city experiences a period of mild rain as well as dampness. Typhoons are uncommon but possible in the late stages of summer and early part of autumn. The annual mean temperature is around 15.91&#160;&#176;C (60.6&#160;&#176;F), with the monthly 24-hour average temperature ranging from 2.7&#160;&#176;C (36.9&#160;&#176;F) in January to 28.1&#160;&#176;C (82.6&#160;&#176;F) in July. Extremes since 1951 have ranged from &#8722;14.0&#160;&#176;C (7&#160;&#176;F) on 6 January 1955 to 40.7&#160;&#176;C (105&#160;&#176;F) on 22 August 1959.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[76]</a></sup> On average precipitation falls 115&#160;days out of the year, and the average annual rainfall is 1,090&#160;mm (43&#160;in). With monthly percent possible sunshine ranging from 37&#160;percent in March to 52&#160;percent in August, the city receives 1,926 hours of bright sunshine annually.\n</p><p>Nanjing is endowed with rich natural resources, which include more than 40 kinds of minerals. Among them, iron and <a href="/wiki/Sulfur" title="Sulfur">sulfur</a> reserves make up 40&#160;percent of those of Jiangsu province. Its reserves of <a href="/wiki/Strontium" title="Strontium">strontium</a> rank first in East Asia and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_East_Asia" title="South East Asia">South East Asia</a> region. Nanjing also possesses abundant water resources, both from the Yangtze River and groundwater. In addition, it has several natural hot springs such as Tangshan Hot Spring in <a href="/wiki/Jiangning_District" title="Jiangning District">Jiangning</a> and Tangquan Hot Spring in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pukou" title="Pukou">Pukou</a>.\n</p><p>\nSun Yat-sen once summarized and lauded the feature of Nanjing in his book <i>The International Development of China</i> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">&#24314;&#22283;&#26041;&#30053;</span>):</p><blockquote><p>Nanking was the old capital of China before Peking, and is situated in a fine locality which comprises high mountains, deep water and a vast level plain&#8212;a rare site to be found in any part of the world. It also lies at the center of a very rich country on both sides of the lower Yangtze. (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">&#21335;&#20140;&#28858;&#20013;&#22283;&#21476;&#37117;&#65292;&#22312;&#21271;&#20140;&#20043;&#21069;&#65292;&#32780;&#20854;&#20301;&#32622;&#20035;&#22312;&#19968;&#32654;&#21892;&#20043;&#22320;&#21312;&#12290;&#20854;&#22320;&#26377;&#39640;&#23665;&#65292;&#26377;&#28145;&#27700;&#65292;&#26377;&#24179;&#21407;&#65292;&#27492;&#19977;&#31278;&#22825;&#24037;&#65292;&#37912;&#27603;&#19968;&#34389;&#65292;&#22312;&#19990;&#30028;&#20013;&#20043;&#22823;&#37117;&#24066;&#35488;&#38627;&#35219;&#22914;&#27492;&#20339;&#22659;&#20063;&#12290;&#32780;&#21448;&#24688;&#23621;&#38263;&#27743;&#19979;&#28216;&#20841;&#23736;&#26368;&#35920;&#23500;&#21312;&#22495;&#20043;&#20013;&#24515;...</span>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[77]</a></sup></p></blockquote><p>To be more exact, surrounded by the Yangtze River and mountains, the urban area of the city enjoys its scenic natural environment. Xuanwu Lake and Mochou Lake are located in the center of the city and are easily accessible to the public, while Purple Mountain is covered with deciduous and coniferous forests preserving various historical and cultural sites. Meanwhile, a Yangtze River deep-water channel is under construction to enable Nanjing to handle the navigation of 50,000 <a href="/wiki/Deadweight_tonnage" title="Deadweight tonnage">DWT</a> vessels from the East China Sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[78]</a></sup></p><div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed" class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chinahaze_tmo_2013341_lrg.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5400" data-file-width="4400" decoding="async" height="295"
