//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Chinahaze_tmo_2013341_lrg.jpg/480px-Chinahaze_tmo_2013341_lrg.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chinahaze_tmo_2013341_lrg.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>7 December 2013 image from <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>\'s Terra Satellite of the Eastern China smog</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/2013_Eastern_China_smog" title="2013 Eastern China smog">2013 Eastern China smog</a></div>\n<p>A dense wave of smog began in the <a href="/wiki/Central_China" title="Central China">central</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_China" title="East China">east</a> parts of China on 2 December 2013 across a distance of around 1,200&#160;km (750&#160;mi),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[80]</a></sup> including Tianjin, Hebei, Shandong, Jiangsu, Anhui, Shanghai and Zhejiang. A lack of cold air flow, combined with slow-moving <a href="/wiki/Air_mass" title="Air mass">air masses</a> carrying industrial emissions, collected <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">airborne pollutants</a> to form a thick layer of smog over the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[81]</a></sup> The heavy smog heavily polluted central and southern Jiangsu Province, especially in and around Nanjing,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wylww_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-wylww-87">[82]</a></sup> with its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_Quality_Index" title="Air Quality Index">AQI pollution Index</a> at "severely polluted" for five straight days and "heavily polluted" for nine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[83]</a></sup> On 3 December 2013, levels of PM<sub>2.5</sub> particulate matter average over 943 micrograms per cubic meter,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xinhua131213XJB_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-xinhua131213XJB-89">[84]</a></sup> falling to over 338 micrograms per cubic meter on 4 December 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[85]</a></sup> Between 3:00 pm, 3 December and 2:00pm, 4 December local time, several expressways from Nanjing to other Jiangsu cities were closed, stranding dozens of passenger buses in Zhongyangmen bus station.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wylww_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-wylww-87">[82]</a></sup> From 5 to 6 December, Nanjing issued a red alert for air pollution and closed down all kindergarten through middle schools. Children\'s Hospital outpatient services increased by 33&#160;percent; general incidence of bronchitis, pneumonia, upper respiratory tract infections significantly increased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[86]</a></sup> The smog dissipated 12 December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ShanghaiGOV131210_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-ShanghaiGOV131210-92">[87]</a></sup> Officials blamed the dense pollution on lack of wind, automobile exhaust emissions under low air pressure, and <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a>-powered <a href="/wiki/District_heating" title="District heating">district heating</a> system in <a href="/wiki/North_China" title="North China">north China</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[88]</a></sup> Prevailing winds blew low-hanging air masses of factory emissions (mostly <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">SO<sub>2</sub></a>) towards China\'s east coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[89]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nanjing_Government.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1068" data-file-width="1750" decoding="async" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Nanjing_Government.jpg/220px-Nanjing_Government.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Nanjing_Government.jpg/330px-Nanjing_Government.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Nanjing_Government.jpg/440px-Nanjing_Government.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nanjing_Government.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>People\'s Government of Nanjing City</div></div></div>\n<p>At present, the full name of the government of Nanjing is "People\'s Government of Nanjing City" and the city is under the one-party rule of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">CPC</a>, with the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=CPC_Nanjing_Committee_Secretary&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="CPC Nanjing Committee Secretary (page does not exist)">CPC Nanjing Committee Secretary</a> as the <i>de facto</i> governor of the city and the mayor as the executive head of the government working under the secretary.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The sub-provincial city of Nanjing is divided into 11 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/District_of_China" title="District of China">districts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[90]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th Q&#363;\n</td>\n<td align="right">419,523\n</td>\n<td align="right">983.00\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Gaochun_District" title="Gaochun District">Gaochun</a>\n</td>\n<td align="left"><span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#39640;&#28147;&#21306;</span>\n</td>\n<td align="left">G&#257;och&#250;n Q&#363;\n</td>\n<td align="right">420,429\n</td>\n<td align="right">801.00\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<ul><li>Defunct districts: <a href="/wiki/Baixia_District" title="Baixia District">Baixia District</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xiaguan_District" title="Xiaguan District">Xiaguan District</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Population_of_Nanking_in_December_of_1937" title="Population of Nanking in December of 1937">Population of Nanking in December of 1937</a></div>\n<table align="right;" border="1" style="float:right; margin: 1em;border-collapse:collapse;">\n<caption><b>Population trend</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[93]</a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<td valign="top">\n<table>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="background:#efefef;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background:#efefef; width:80px;">Residents (in million)\n</th>\n<th style="background:#efefef; width:100px;">natural growth rate (%)\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1949</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2.5670</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">13.09\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1950</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2.5670</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">15.64\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1955</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2.8034</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">19.94\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1960</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">3.2259</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">0.23\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1965</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">3.4529</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">25.58\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1970</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">3.6053</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">20.76\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1975</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">3.9299</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">9.53\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1978</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">4.1238</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">8.84\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1990</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">5.0182</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">9.18\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td>\n<td valign="top">\n<table>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="background:#efefef;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background:#efefef; width:80px;">Residents (in million)\n</th>\n<th style="background:#efefef; width:100px;">natural growth rate (%)\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1995</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">5.2172</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2.62\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1996</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">5.2543</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2.63\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1997</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">5.2982</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2.16\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1998</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">5.3231</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1.00\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1999</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">5.3744</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2.01\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2000</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">5.4489</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2.48\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2001</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">5.5304</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1.60\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2002</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">5.6328</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">0.70\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2003</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">5.7223</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1.50\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2006</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">6.0700</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">6.11\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>At the time of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_PRC_census" title="2010 PRC census">2010 census</a>, the total population of the City of Nanjing was 8.005&#160;million. The <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> estimated the encompassing <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a> at the time as 11.7 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oecd2015_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-oecd2015-2">[2]</a></sup> Official statistics in 2011 estimated the city\'s population to be 8.11&#160;million. The <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a> was 8.86&#160;percent and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Death_rate" title="Death rate">death rate</a> was 6.88&#160;percent. The urban area had a population of 6.47&#160;million people. The <a href="/wiki/Sex_ratio" title="Sex ratio">sex ratio</a> of the city population was 107.31 males to 100 females.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[95]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As in most of eastern China the official ethnic makeup of Nanjing is predominantly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Han_nationality" title="Han nationality">Han nationality</a> (98.56&#160;percent), with 50 other <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_minorities_in_China" title="Ethnic minorities in China">official ethnic groups</a>. In 1999, 77,394 residents belonged to officially defined minorities, among which the vast majority (64,832) were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hui_Chinese" title="Hui Chinese">Hui</a>, contributing 83.76&#160;percent to the minority population. The second and third largest minority groups were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchu" title="Manchu">Manchu</a> (2,311) and <a href="/wiki/Zhuang_people" title="Zhuang people">Zhuang</a> (533). Most of the minority nationalities resided in Jianye District, comprising 9.13&#160;percent of the district\'s population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[96]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Earlier_development">Earlier development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Earlier development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There was a massive cultivating in the area of Nanjing from the Three Kingdoms period to Southern dynasties. The sparse population led to land as royal rewards were granted for rules&#8217; people. At first, the landless peasants benefited from it, then the senior officials and aristocratic families. Since large numbers of immigrants flooded into the area, reclamation was quite common in its remote parts, which promoted its agricultural development.\n</p><p>The craft industries, by contrast, had a faster growth. Especially the textiles section, there were about 200,000 craftsmen by the late Qing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[97]</a></sup> Several dynasties established their imperial textiles bureaus in Nanjing. The Nanjing Brocade (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#21335;&#20140;&#20113;&#38182;</span>) is their exquisite product as the cloth for the royal garments such as <a href="/wiki/Dragon_robe" title="Dragon robe">dragon robes</a>. Meanwhile, the satins from Nanjing were called &#8220;tribute satins&#8221; ("<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#36129;&#32526;</span>"), because they were usually paid as tribute to the monarchy. Besides, minting, papermaking, shipbuilding grew initially since the Three Kingdoms period. As Nanjing was the capital of the Ming dynasty, the industries further expanded, where both state-owned and numerous private businesses served the imperial court. Several place names in Nanjing remains witnessed them, such as Wangjinshi (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#32593;&#24062;&#24066;</span>, the market sells <a href="/wiki/Wangjin" title="Wangjin">wangjin</a>), Guyilang (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#20272;&#34915;&#24266;</span>, the corridor for garments bargain), Youfangqiao (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#27833;&#22346;&#26725;</span>, the bridge near an oil mill).\n</p><p>Moreover, the trade in Nanjing was also flourishing. The Ming dynasty drawing <i>Prosperous Nanjing</i> (<span lang="zh-Hans"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%8D%97%E9%83%BD" title="wikt:&#21335;&#37117;">&#21335;&#37117;</a><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E7%B9%81%E4%BC%9A" title="wikt:&#32321;&#20250;">&#32321;&#20250;</a><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%9B%BE%E5%8D%B7" title="wikt:&#22270;&#21367;">&#22270;&#21367;</a></span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">N&#225;nd&#363; F&#225;nhu&#236; T&#250;ju&#462;n</span></i>) depicts a vivid market scene bustling with people and full of various sorts of shops. However, the economic developments were almost wiped out by the Taiping Rebellion\'s catastrophe.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_times">Modern times</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Modern times">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Into the first half of the twentieth century after the establishment of ROC, Nanjing gradually shifted from being a production hub towards being a heavy consumption city, mainly because of the rapid expansion of its wealthy population after Nanjing once again regained the political spotlight of China. A number of huge <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_stores" title="Department stores">department stores</a> such as <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Zhongyang_Shangchang&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Zhongyang Shangchang (page does not exist)">Zhongyang Shangchang</a> sprouted up, attracting merchants from all over China to sell their products in Nanjing. In 1933, the revenue generated by the food and entertainment industry in the city exceeded the sum of the output of the manufacturing and agriculture industry. One third of the city population worked in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Service_industry" title="Service industry">service industry</a>, .\n</p><p>In the 1950s after PRC was established by CPC, the government invested heavily in the city to build a series of state-owned <a href="/wiki/Heavy_industry" title="Heavy industry">heavy industries</a>, as part of the national plan of rapid <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrialization" title="Industrialization">industrialization</a>, converting it into a heavy industry production center of east China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[98]</a></sup> Overenthusiastic in building a &#8220;world-class&#8221; industrial city, the government also made many disastrous mistakes during development, such as spending hundreds of millions of yuan to mine for non-existent coal, resulting in negative economic growth in the late 1960s. From the 1960s to 1980s there were Five Pillar Industries, namely, electronics, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobile" title="Automobile">cars</a>, petrochemical, iron and steel, and power, each with big state-owned firms. After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reform_and_Opening" title="Reform and Opening">Reform and Opening</a> recovering market economy, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State-owned_enterprises" title="State-owned enterprises">state-owned enterprises</a> found themselves incapable of competing with efficient multinational firms and local private firms, hence were either mired in heavy debt or forced into <a href="/wiki/Bankruptcy" title="Bankruptcy">bankruptcy</a> or <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">privatization</a> and this resulted in large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Layoff" title="Layoff">layoff workers</a> who were technically not unemployed but effectively jobless.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Today">Today</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Today">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nanjing_Xinjiekou_Skyline.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1986" data-file-width="3533" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Nanjing_Xinjiekou_Skyline.jpg/220px-Nanjing_Xinjiekou_Skyline.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Nanjing_Xinjiekou_Skyline.jpg/330px-Nanjing_Xinjiekou_Skyline.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Nanjing_Xinjiekou_Skyline.jpg/440px-Nanjing_Xinjiekou_Skyline.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nanjing_Xinjiekou_Skyline.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Skyline of Nanjing\'s Xinjiekou district as seen from Nanjing University\'s Gulou campus.</div></div></div>\n<p>The current economy of the city is basically newly developed based on the past. Service industries are dominating, accounting for about 60 percent of the GDP of the city, and financial industry, culture industry and tourism industry are top 3 of them. Industries of information technology, energy saving and environmental protection, new energy, smart power grid and intelligent equipment manufacturing have become pillar industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[99]</a></sup> Big <a href="/wiki/Civilian-run_enterprise" title="Civilian-run enterprise">civilian-run enterprise</a> include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suning_Commerce_Group" title="Suning Commerce Group">Suning Commerce</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yurun" title="Yurun">Yurun</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sanpower&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sanpower (page does not exist)">Sanpower</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fuzhong&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fuzhong (page does not exist)">Fuzhong</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hiteker&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hiteker (page does not exist)">Hiteker</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=5stars&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="5stars (page does not exist)">5stars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jinpu" title="Jinpu">Jinpu</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiandi" title="Tiandi">Tiandi</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=CTTQ_Pharmaceutical&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="CTTQ Pharmaceutical (page does not exist)">CTTQ Pharmaceutical</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Iron_and_Steel_Company" title="Nanjing Iron and Steel Company">Nanjing Iron and Steel Company</a> and <a href="/wiki/Simcere_Pharmaceutical" title="Simcere Pharmaceutical">Simcere Pharmaceutical</a>. Big state-owned firms include <a href="/wiki/Panda_Electronics" title="Panda Electronics">Panda Electronics</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Yangzi_Petrochemical&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Yangzi Petrochemical (page does not exist)">Yangzi Petrochemical</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jinling_Petrochemical&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jinling Petrochemical (page does not exist)">Jinling Petrochemical</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing_Chemical&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nanjing Chemical (page does not exist)">Nanjing Chemical</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jincheng_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jincheng Motors (page does not exist)">Jincheng Motors</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jinling_Pharmaceutical&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jinling Pharmaceutical (page does not exist)">Jinling Pharmaceutical</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chenguang" title="Chenguang">Chenguang</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=NARI_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="NARI Group (page does not exist)">NARI</a>. The city has also attracted foreign investment, <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational firms</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ericsson" title="Ericsson">Ericsson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iveco" title="Iveco">Iveco</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A.O._Smith" title="A.O. Smith">A.O. Smith</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sharp_Corporation" title="Sharp Corporation">Sharp</a> have established their lines, and a number of multinationals such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ford" title="Ford">Ford</a>, <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lucent" title="Lucent">Lucent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">Samsung</a> and <a href="/wiki/SAP_SE" title="SAP SE">SAP</a> established research center there. Many China-based leading firms such as <a href="/wiki/Huawei" title="Huawei">Huawei</a>, <a href="/wiki/ZTE" title="ZTE">ZTE</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lenovo" title="Lenovo">Lenovo</a> have key R &amp; D institutes in the city. Nanjing is an industrial technology research and development hub, hosting many R &amp; D centers and institutions, especially in areas of electronics technology, information technology, computer software, biotechnology and pharmaceutical technology and new material technology.\n</p><p>In recent years, Nanjing has been developing its economy, commerce, industry, as well as city construction. In 2013 the city\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP" title="GDP">GDP</a> was RMB 801&#160;billion (3rd in Jiangsu), and GDP per capita(current price) was RMB 98,174(US$16041), an 11&#160;percent increase from 2012. The average urban resident\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disposable_income" title="Disposable income">disposable income</a> was RMB 36,200, while the average rural resident\'s net income was RMB 14,513. The registered urban <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unemployment_rate" title="Unemployment rate">unemployment rate</a> was 3.02&#160;percent, lower than the national average (4.3&#160;percent). Nanjing\'s Gross Domestic Product ranked 12th in 2013 in China, and its overall competence ranked 6th in mainland and 8th including Taiwan and <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[100]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width: -moz-min-content; width: -webkit-min-content; width: min-content; max-width: 100%;"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow: auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E5%8D%97%E4%BA%AC%E5%85%A8%E6%99%AF.jpg" title="A panoramic view of Nanjing in 2005"><img alt="" data-file-height="461" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/%E5%8D%97%E4%BA%AC%E5%85%A8%E6%99%AF.jpg/1111px-%E5%8D%97%E4%BA%AC%E5%85%A8%E6%99%AF.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/%E5%8D%97%E4%BA%AC%E5%85%A8%E6%99%AF.jpg/1666px-%E5%8D%97%E4%BA%AC%E5%85%A8%E6%99%AF.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/48/%E5%8D%97%E4%BA%AC%E5%85%A8%E6%99%AF.jpg 2x" width="1111"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%E5%8D%97%E4%BA%AC%E5%85%A8%E6%99%AF.jpg" title="File:&#21335;&#20140;&#20840;&#26223;.jpg"> </a></div><center>A panoramic view of Nanjing in 2005</center></div></div></div>\n<dl><dt>Industrial zones</dt></dl>\n<p>There are a number of industrial zones in Nanjing.\n</p>\n<ul><li><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20010509143259/http://www.njnhz.gov.cn/" rel="nofollow">Nanjing New and High-Tech Industry Development Zone</a></li>\n<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.bxgxq.com/" rel="nofollow">Nanjing Baixia Hi-Tech Industrial Zone</a></li>\n<li><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160224113926/http://www.njxg.com/" rel="nofollow">Nanjing Economic and Technological Development Zone</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Nanjing is the transportation hub in eastern China and the downstream Yangtze River area. Different means of transportation constitute a three-dimensional transport system that includes land, water and air. As in most other Chinese cities, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_transportation" title="Public transportation">public transportation</a> is the dominant mode of travel of the majority of the citizens. As of October 2014, Nanjing had <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River_bridges_and_tunnels" title="Yangtze River bridges and tunnels">four bridges and two tunnels</a> over the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze River</a>, which are tying districts north of the river with the city center on the south bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yangtze_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yangtze-106">[101]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:South_Nanjing_Station_2011.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2250" data-file-width="3376" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/South_Nanjing_Station_2011.JPG/220px-South_Nanjing_Station_2011.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/South_Nanjing_Station_2011.JPG/330px-South_Nanjing_Station_2011.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/South_Nanjing_Station_2011.JPG/440px-South_Nanjing_Station_2011.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:South_Nanjing_Station_2011.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nanjing South Railway Station</div></div></div>\n<p>Nanjing is an important railway hub in eastern China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[102]</a></sup> It serves as rail junction for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jinghu_Railway" title="Jinghu Railway">Beijing-Shanghai (Jinghu)</a> (which is itself composed of the old <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jinpu_Railway" title="Jinpu Railway">Jinpu</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huning_Railway" title="Huning Railway">Huning Railways</a>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanjing%E2%80%93Tongling_Railway" title="Nanjing&#8211;Tongling Railway">Nanjing&#8211;Tongling Railway (Ningtong)</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanjing%E2%80%93Qidong_Railway" title="Nanjing&#8211;Qidong Railway">Nanjing&#8211;Qidong (Ningqi)</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanjing%E2%80%93Xian_Railway" title="Nanjing&#8211;Xian Railway">Nanjing-Xian (Ningxi)</a> which encompasses the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hefei%E2%80%93Nanjing_Passenger_Railway" title="Hefei&#8211;Nanjing Passenger Railway">Hefei&#8211;Nanjing Railway</a>.\nNanjing is connected to the <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_China#Track_Network" title="High-speed rail in China">national high-speed railway network</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Shanghai_High-Speed_Railway" title="Beijing&#8211;Shanghai High-Speed Railway">Beijing&#8211;Shanghai High-Speed Railway</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai%E2%80%93Wuhan%E2%80%93Chengdu_Passenger_Dedicated_Line" title="Shanghai&#8211;Wuhan&#8211;Chengdu Passenger Dedicated Line">Shanghai&#8211;Wuhan&#8211;Chengdu Passenger Dedicated Line</a>, with several more high-speed rail lines under construction.\n</p><p>Among all 17 railway stations in Nanjing, passenger rail service is mainly provided by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanjing_Railway_Station" title="Nanjing Railway Station">Nanjing Railway Station</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanjing_South_Railway_Station" title="Nanjing South Railway Station">Nanjing South Railway Station</a>, while other stations like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanjing_West_Railway_Station" title="Nanjing West Railway Station">Nanjing West Railway Station</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zhonghuamen_Railway_Station" title="Zhonghuamen Railway Station">Zhonghuamen Railway Station</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xianlin_Railway_Station" title="Xianlin Railway Station">Xianlin Railway Station</a> serve minor roles. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanjing_Railway_Station" title="Nanjing Railway Station">Nanjing Railway Station</a> was first built in 1968.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-&#21335;&#20140;&#28779;&#36710;&#31449;_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-&#21335;&#20140;&#28779;&#36710;&#31449;-108">[103]</a></sup> On November 12, 1999, the station was burnt in a serious fire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[104]</a></sup> Reconstruction of the station was finished on September 1, 2005. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanjing_South_Railway_Station" title="Nanjing South Railway Station">Nanjing South Railway Station</a>, which is one of the 5 hub stations on Beijing&#8211;Shanghai High-Speed Railway, has officially been claimed as the largest railway station in Asia and the second largest in the world in terms of GFA (Gross Floor Area).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[105]</a></sup> Construction of Nanjing South Station began on 10 January 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[106]</a></sup> The station was opened for public service in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[107]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nanjing_Yangtze_River_Bridge.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Nanjing_Yangtze_River_Bridge.jpg/220px-Nanjing_Yangtze_River_Bridge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Nanjing_Yangtze_River_Bridge.jpg/330px-Nanjing_Yangtze_River_Bridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Nanjing_Yangtze_River_Bridge.jpg/440px-Nanjing_Yangtze_River_Bridge.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nanjing_Yangtze_River_Bridge.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Yangtze_River_Bridge" title="Nanjing Yangtze River Bridge">Nanjing Yangtze River Bridge</a>, built in 1968,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-&#21335;&#20140;&#28779;&#36710;&#31449;_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-&#21335;&#20140;&#28779;&#36710;&#31449;-108">[103]</a></sup> the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River_bridges_and_tunnels" title="Yangtze River bridges and tunnels">bridge over the Yangtze River</a> to be built without foreign assistance.</div></div></div>\n<p>As an important regional hub in the <a href="/wiki/Yangtze_River_Delta" title="Yangtze River Delta">Yangtze River Delta</a>, Nanjing is well-connected by over 60 state and provincial highways to all parts of China.\n</p><p>Express highways such as Hu&#8211;Ning, Ning&#8211;He, Ning&#8211;Hang enable commuters to travel to Shanghai, <a href="/wiki/Hefei" title="Hefei">Hefei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hangzhou" title="Hangzhou">Hangzhou</a>, and other important cities quickly and conveniently. Inside the city of Nanjing, there are 230&#160;km (140&#160;mi) of highways, with a highway coverage density of 3.38&#160;kilometers per hundred square&#160;kilometers (5.44&#160;mi/100&#160;sq&#160;mi). The total road coverage density of the city is 112.56&#160;kilometers per hundred square&#160;kilometers (181.15&#160;mi/100&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-&#25968;&#23383;&#20132;&#36890;_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-&#25968;&#23383;&#20132;&#36890;-113">[108]</a></sup> The two artery roads in Nanjing are Zhongshan Road and Hanzhong. The two roads cross in the city center, Xinjiekou.\n</p><p><b>Expressways</b>&#65371;G+XXxx&#65288;National Express,&#22269;&#23478;&#39640;&#36895;&#65289;&#65292;S+XX&#65288;&#30465;&#32423;&#39640;&#36895;&#65289;&#65373;:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/G25_Changchun%E2%80%93Shenzhen_Expressway" title="G25 Changchun&#8211;Shenzhen Expressway">G25 Changchun&#8211;Shenzhen Expressway</a>&#65288;&#38271;&#28145;&#39640;&#36895;&#25110;&#23425;&#26477;&#39640;&#36895;&#65289;</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/G36_Nanjing%E2%80%93Luoyang_Expressway" title="G36 Nanjing&#8211;Luoyang Expressway">G36 Nanjing&#8211;Luoyang Expressway</a>&#65288;&#23425;&#27931;&#39640;&#36895;&#65289;</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/G40_Shanghai%E2%80%93Xi%27an_Expressway" title="G40 Shanghai&#8211;Xi\'an Expressway">G40 Shanghai&#8211;Xi\'an Expressway</a>&#65288;&#27818;&#38485;&#39640;&#36895;&#65289;</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/G42_Shanghai%E2%80%93Chengdu_Expressway" title="G42 Shanghai&#8211;Chengdu Expressway">G42 Shanghai&#8211;Chengdu Expressway</a>&#65288;&#27818;&#33993;&#39640;&#36895;&#25110;&#27818;&#23425;&#39640;&#36895;&#65289;</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/G4211_Nanjing%E2%80%93Wuhu_Expressway" title="G4211 Nanjing&#8211;Wuhu Expressway">G4211 Nanjing&#8211;Wuhu Expressway</a>, a spur of G42 that extends west to <a href="/wiki/Wuhu" title="Wuhu">Wuhu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anhui" title="Anhui">Anhui</a>&#65288;&#23425;&#33436;&#39640;&#36895;&#65289;</li>\n<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=S55_Nanjing%E2%80%93Gaochun%EF%BC%88Xuancheng%EF%BC%89_Expressway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="S55 Nanjing&#8211;Gaochun&#65288;Xuancheng&#65289; Expressway (page does not exist)">S55 Nanjing&#8211;Gaochun&#65288;Xuancheng&#65289; Expressway</a>&#65288;&#23425;&#23459;&#39640;&#36895;&#25110;&#21335;&#20140;&#26426;&#22330;&#39640;&#36895;&#65289;</li>\n<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=S38_Yanjiang_Expressway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="S38 Yanjiang Expressway (page does not exist)">S38 Yanjiang Expressway</a>&#65288;&#27839;&#27743;&#39640;&#36895;&#25110;&#24120;&#21512;&#39640;&#36895;&#65289;</li>\n<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=G2501_Nanjing_Ring_Expressway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="G2501 Nanjing Ring Expressway (page does not exist)">G2501 Nanjing Ring Expressway</a>&#65288;&#26032;&#21335;&#20140;&#32469;&#22478;&#39640;&#36895;&#25110;&#21335;&#20140;&#32469;&#36234;&#39640;&#36895;&#65289;</li>\n<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=S001_Nanjing_Ring_Highway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="S001 Nanjing Ring Highway (page does not exist)">S001 Nanjing Ring Highway</a>&#65288;&#26087;&#21335;&#20140;&#32469;&#22478;&#39640;&#36895;&#25110;&#21335;&#20140;&#32469;&#22478;&#20844;&#36335;&#65289;</li></ul>\n<p><b>National Highway</b> &#65371;G1xx&#65288;which starts from Beijing &#65289;, G2xx&#65288;north-south&#65289;&#65292;G3xx&#65288;west-east&#65289;&#65373;:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/China_National_Highway_104" title="China National Highway 104">China National Highway 104</a>&#8212;motorists can either drive northwest to <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> or south to <a href="/wiki/Fuzhou" title="Fuzhou">Fuzhou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/China_National_Highway_205" title="China National Highway 205">China National Highway 205</a>&#8212;motorists can either drive north to <a href="/wiki/Shanhaiguan_District" title="Shanhaiguan District">Shanhaiguan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hebei" title="Hebei">Hebei</a> or south to <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen" title="Shenzhen">Shenzhen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/China_National_Highway_312" title="China National Highway 312">China National Highway 312</a>&#8212;motorists can either drive east to <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a> or west to <a href="/wiki/Khorgas" title="Khorgas">Khorgas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a> on the Kazakh border</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/China_National_Highway_328" title="China National Highway 328">China National Highway 328</a>&#8212;Nanjing is the western terminus of G328, which motorists can follow to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hai%27an_County" title="Hai\'an County">Hai\'an County</a> in eastern Jiangsu</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transportation">Public transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Public transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Metro" title="Nanjing Metro">Nanjing Metro</a></div>\n<p>The city also boasts an efficient network of public transportation, which mainly consists of bus, taxi and metro systems. The bus network, which is currently run by three companies since 2011, provides more than 370 routes covering all parts of the city and suburban areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[109]</a></sup> At present, the <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Metro" title="Nanjing Metro">Nanjing Metro</a> system has a grand total of 377&#160;km (234&#160;mi) of route and 173 stations across 10 lines. They are Line 1, Line 2, Line 3, Line 4, Line 10, Line S1, Line S3, Line S7, Line S8 and Line S9. The city is planning to complete a 17-line Metro and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light-rail" title="Light-rail">light-rail</a> system by 2030.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[110]</a></sup> The expansion of the Metro network will greatly facilitate the intracity transportation and reduce the currently heavy traffic congestion.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Nanjing\'s airport, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lukou_International_Airport" title="Lukou International Airport">Lukou International Airport</a>, serves both national and international flights. In 2013, Nanjing airport handled 15,011,792 passengers and 255,788.6 tonnes of freight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[111]</a></sup> The airport currently has 85 routes to national and international destinations, which include Japan,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[112]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[114]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, United States<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[115]</a></sup> and Germany. The airport is connected by a 29-kilometer (18&#160;mi) highway directly to the city center, and is also linked to various intercity highways, making it accessible to the passengers from the surrounding cities. A railway <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ninggao_Intercity_Rail_Line" title="Ninggao Intercity Rail Line">Ninggao Intercity Line</a> has been built to link the airport with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanjing_South_Railway_Station" title="Nanjing South Railway Station">Nanjing South Railway Station</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[116]</a></sup> Lukou Airport was opened on 28 June 1997, replacing <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Dajiaochang_Airport" title="Nanjing Dajiaochang Airport">Nanjing Dajiaochang Airport</a> as the main airport serving Nanjing. Dajiaochang Airport is still used as a military air base.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nje_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-nje-122">[117]</a></sup>And now Nanjing has another airport&#65293;&#65293;Nanjing Ma\'an International Airport which will temporarily serve as a dual-use military and civil airport.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Nanjing" title="Port of Nanjing">Port of Nanjing</a> is the largest inland port in China, with annual cargo tonnage reached 191,970,000&#160;t in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[118]</a></sup> The port area is 98&#160;km (61&#160;mi) in length and has 64 berths including 16 berths for ships with a tonnage of more than 10,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[119]</a></sup> Nanjing is also the biggest container port along the Yangtze River; in March 2004, the one million container-capacity base, Longtan Containers Port Area opened, further consolidating Nanjing as the leading port in the region. As of  2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it operated six public ports and three industrial ports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[120]</a></sup> The Yangtze River\'s 12.5-meter-deep waterway enables 50,000-ton-class ocean ships directly arrive at the Nanjing Port, and the ocean ships with the capacities of 100,000 tons or above can also reach the port after load reduction in the Yangtze River\'s high-tide period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[121]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Yangtze_River_crossings">Yangtze River crossings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Yangtze River crossings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River_bridges_and_tunnels" title="Yangtze River bridges and tunnels">Yangtze River bridges and tunnels</a></div>\n<p>In the 1960s, the first <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Yangtze_River_Bridge" title="Nanjing Yangtze River Bridge">Nanjing Yangtze River Bridge</a> was completed, and served as the only bridge crossing over the Lower Yangtze in eastern China at that time. The bridge was a source of pride and an important symbol of modern China, having been built and designed by the Chinese themselves following failed surveys by other nations and the reliance on and then rejection of Soviet expertise. Begun in 1960 and opened to traffic in 1968, the bridge is a two-tiered road and rail design spanning 4,600&#160;meters on the upper deck, with approximately 1,580&#160;meters spanning the river itself.  Since then four more bridges and two tunnels have been built.  Going in the downstream direction, the Yangtze crossings in Nanjing are: <a href="/wiki/Dashengguan_Yangtze_River_Bridge" title="Dashengguan Yangtze River Bridge">Dashengguan Bridge</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Line_10,_Nanjing_Metro" title="Line 10, Nanjing Metro">Line 10 Metro Tunnel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Third_Nanjing_Yangtze_Bridge" title="Third Nanjing Yangtze Bridge">Third Bridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Yangtze_River_Tunnel" title="Nanjing Yangtze River Tunnel">Nanjing Yangtze River Tunnel</a>&#65288;&#21335;&#20140;&#38271;&#27743;&#38567;&#36947;&#65289;, First Bridge, <a href="/wiki/Second_Nanjing_Yangtze_Bridge" title="Second Nanjing Yangtze Bridge">Second Bridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Nanjing_Yangtze_Bridge" title="Fourth Nanjing Yangtze Bridge">Fourth Bridge</a>,Nanjing Yangtze Tunnel &#65288;&#21335;&#20140;&#25196;&#23376;&#27743;&#38567;&#36947;&#65289;.In the near future, Such Yangtze Crossings will be added as follow :Jianning West Rd. Tunnel ,Xianxin Rd. Tunnel, Heyan Rd. Tunnel, Fifth Nanjing Yangtze Bridge.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_art">Culture and art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Culture and art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nanjing_library_new1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Nanjing_library_new1.jpg/220px-Nanjing_library_new1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Nanjing_library_new1.jpg/330px-Nanjing_library_new1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Nanjing_library_new1.jpg/440px-Nanjing_library_new1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nanjing_library_new1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Library" title="Nanjing Library">Nanjing Library</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Being one of the four ancient capitals of China, Nanjing has always been a cultural center attracting intellectuals from all over the country. In the <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song</a> dynasties, Nanjing was a place where poets gathered and composed poems reminiscent of its luxurious past; during the <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing</a> dynasties, the city was the official <a href="/wiki/Imperial_examination" title="Imperial examination">imperial examination</a> center (<a href="/wiki/Jiangnan_Examination_Hall" title="Jiangnan Examination Hall">Jiangnan Examination Hall</a>) for the <a href="/wiki/Jiangnan" title="Jiangnan">Jiangnan</a> region, again acting as a hub where different thoughts and opinions converged and thrived.\n</p><p>Today, with a long cultural tradition and strong support from local educational institutions, Nanjing is commonly viewed as a &#8220;city of culture&#8221; and one of the more pleasant cities to live in China.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Nanjing_Art_Groups" title="List of Nanjing Art Groups">List of Nanjing Art Groups</a></div>\n<p>Some of the leading art groups of China are based in Nanjing; they include the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Qianxian_Dance_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Qianxian Dance Company (page does not exist)">Qianxian Dance Company</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing_Dance_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nanjing Dance Company (page does not exist)">Nanjing Dance Company</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jiangsu_Peking_Opera_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jiangsu Peking Opera Institute (page does not exist)">Jiangsu Peking Opera Institute</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing_Xiaohonghua_Art_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nanjing Xiaohonghua Art Company (page does not exist)">Nanjing Xiaohonghua Art Company</a> among others.\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jiangsu_Province_Kun_Opera" title="Jiangsu Province Kun Opera">Jiangsu Province Kun Opera</a> is one of the best theaters for <a href="/wiki/Kunqu" title="Kunqu">Kunqu</a>, China\'s oldest stage art.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[122]</a></sup>\nIt is considered a conservative and traditional troupe. Nanjing also has professional opera troupes for the Yang, Yue (shaoxing), Xi and Jing (Chinese opera varieties) as well as Suzhou pingtan, spoken theater and puppet theater.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jiangsu_Art_Gallery" title="Jiangsu Art Gallery">Jiangsu Art Gallery</a> is the largest gallery in Jiangsu Province, presenting some of the best traditional and contemporary art pieces of China like the historical Master <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ho-Kan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ho-Kan (page does not exist)">Ho-Kan</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[123]</a></sup> many other smaller-scale galleries, such as <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Red_Chamber_Art_Garden&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Red Chamber Art Garden (page does not exist)">Red Chamber Art Garden</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jinling_Stone_Gallery&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jinling Stone Gallery (page does not exist)">Jinling Stone Gallery</a>, also have their own special exhibitions.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Festivals_and_Events_of_Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="List of Festivals and Events of Nanjing (page does not exist)">List of Festivals and Events of Nanjing</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PlumBlossomFestival.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4208" data-file-width="2368" decoding="async" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/PlumBlossomFestival.jpg/120px-PlumBlossomFestival.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/PlumBlossomFestival.jpg/180px-PlumBlossomFestival.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/PlumBlossomFestival.jpg/240px-PlumBlossomFestival.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PlumBlossomFestival.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An elderly man sketches plum blossoms at the festival.</div></div></div>\n<p>Many traditional festivals and customs were observed in the old times, which included climbing the City Wall on January 16, bathing in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Qing_Xi_of_Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Qing Xi of Nanjing (page does not exist)">Qing Xi</a> on March 3, hill hiking on September 9 and others (the dates are in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_lunar_calendar" title="Chinese lunar calendar">Chinese lunar calendar</a>). Almost none of them, however, are still celebrated by modern Nanjingese.\n</p><p>Instead, Nanjing, as a popular tourist destination, hosts a series of government-organized events throughout the year. The annual <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=International_Plum_Blossom_Festival&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="International Plum Blossom Festival (page does not exist)">International Plum Blossom Festival</a> held in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Plum_Blossom_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Plum Blossom Hill (page does not exist)">Plum Blossom Hill</a>, the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plum_blossom" title="Plum blossom">plum collection</a> in China, attracts thousands of tourists both domestically and internationally. Other events include Nanjing Baima Peach Blossom and Kite Festival, <a href="/wiki/Jiangxin_Island" title="Jiangxin Island">Jiangxin Zhou</a> Fruit Festival and Linggu Temple Sweet Osmanthus Festival.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Library" title="Nanjing Library">Nanjing Library</a>, founded in 1907, houses more than 10 million volumes of printed materials and is the third largest library in China, after the <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_China" title="National Library of China">National Library</a> in Beijing and <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Library" title="Shanghai Library">Shanghai Library</a>. Other libraries, such as city-owned <a href="/wiki/Jinling_Library" title="Jinling Library">Jinling Library</a> and various district libraries, also provide considerable amount of information to citizens. <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_University_Library" title="Nanjing University Library">Nanjing University Library</a> is the second largest university libraries in China after Peking University Library, and the fifth largest nationwide, especially in the number of precious collections.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nanjing_Museum_big.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1168" data-file-width="1752" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Nanjing_Museum_big.jpg/220px-Nanjing_Museum_big.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Nanjing_Museum_big.jpg/330px-Nanjing_Museum_big.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Nanjing_Museum_big.jpg/440px-Nanjing_Museum_big.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nanjing_Museum_big.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Museum" title="Nanjing Museum">Nanjing Museum</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For a more comprehensive list, see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Nanjing" title="List of museums in Nanjing">List of museums in Nanjing</a>.</div>\n<p>Nanjing has some of the oldest and finest museums in China. <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Museum" title="Nanjing Museum">Nanjing Museum</a>, formerly known as National Central Museum during ROC period, is the first modern museum and remains as one of the leading museums in China having 400,000 items in its permanent collection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-museum_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-museum-129">[124]</a></sup> The museum is notable for enormous collections of Ming and Qing imperial porcelain, which is among the largest in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[125]</a></sup>\nOther museums include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_Museum_of_Nanjing" title="City Museum of Nanjing">City Museum of Nanjing</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Chaotian_Palace" title="Chaotian Palace">Chaotian Palace</a>, the Oriental Metropolitan Museum,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[f]</a></sup> the China Modern History Museum in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidential_Building_(Nanjing)" title="Presidential Building (Nanjing)">Presidential Palace</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanjing_Massacre_Memorial_Hall" title="Nanjing Massacre Memorial Hall">Nanjing Massacre Memorial Hall</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiping_Kingdom_History_Museum" title="Taiping Kingdom History Museum">Taiping Kingdom History Museum</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jiangning_Imperial_Silk_Manufacturing_Museum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jiangning Imperial Silk Manufacturing Museum (page does not exist)">Jiangning Imperial Silk Manufacturing Museum</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[g]</a></sup> Nanjing <a href="/wiki/Yunjin" title="Yunjin">Yunjin</a> Museum, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing_City_Wall_Cultural_Museum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nanjing City Wall Cultural Museum (page does not exist)">Nanjing City Wall Cultural Museum</a>, Nanjing Customs Museum in Ganxi House,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[h]</a></sup> Nanjing Astronomical History Museum, Nanjing Paleontological Museum, Nanjing Geological Museum, Nanjing Riverstones Museum, and other museums and memorials such <a href="/wiki/Zheng_He" title="Zheng He">Zheng He</a> Memorial<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[i]</a></sup> Jinling Four Modern Calligraphers Memorial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[j]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theater">Theater</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Theater">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Most of Nanjing\'s major theaters are multi-purpose, used as convention halls, cinemas, musical halls and theaters on different occasions. The major theaters include the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing_People%27s_Convention_Hall&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nanjing People\'s Convention Hall (page does not exist)">People\'s Convention Hall</a> and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing_Arts_and_Culture_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nanjing Arts and Culture Center (page does not exist)">Nanjing Arts and Culture Center</a>. The Capital Theater well known in the past is now a museum in theater/film.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Night_life">Night life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Night life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fuzimiaonight.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Fuzimiaonight.JPG/220px-Fuzimiaonight.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Fuzimiaonight.JPG/330px-Fuzimiaonight.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Fuzimiaonight.JPG/440px-Fuzimiaonight.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fuzimiaonight.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Qinhuai River</div></div></div>\n<p>Traditionally Nanjing\'s nightlife was mostly centered around <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Fuzimiao" title="Nanjing Fuzimiao">Nanjing Fuzimiao</a> (Confucius Temple) area along the <a href="/wiki/Qinhuai_River" title="Qinhuai River">Qinhuai River</a>, where night markets, restaurants and pubs thrived.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[127]</a></sup> Boating at night in the river was a main attraction of the city. Thus, one can see the statues of the famous teachers and educators of the past not too far from those of the courtesans who educated the young men in the other arts.\n</p><p>In the past 20&#160;years, several commercial streets have been developed, hence the nightlife has become more diverse: there are shopping malls opening late in the <a href="/wiki/Xinjiekou,_Nanjing" title="Xinjiekou, Nanjing">Xinjiekou</a> CBD and <a href="/wiki/Hunan_Road_Commercial_Street" title="Hunan Road Commercial Street">Hunan Road</a>. The well-established "<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing_1912&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nanjing 1912 (page does not exist)">Nanjing 1912</a>" district hosts a wide variety of recreational facilities ranging from traditional restaurants and western pubs to dance clubs. There are two major areas where bars are densely located; one is in 1912 block; the other is along Shanghai road and its neighborhood. Both are popular with international residents of the city.\n</p><p>Local people still very much enjoy street food, such as lamb <a href="/wiki/Kebab" title="Kebab">kebabs</a>. As elsewhere in Asia, <a href="/wiki/Karaoke" title="Karaoke">karaoke</a> is popular with both young and old crowds.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_and_symbolism">Food and symbolism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Food and symbolism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Many of the city\'s local favorite dishes are based on ducks, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanjing_salted_duck" title="Nanjing salted duck">Nanjing salted duck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duck_blood_and_vermicelli_soup" title="Duck blood and vermicelli soup">duck blood and vermicelli soup</a>, and duck oil pancake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[128]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The radish is also a typical food representing people of Nanjing, which has been spread through word of mouth as an interesting fact for many years in China. According to Nanjing.GOV.cn, "There is a long history of growing radish in Nanjing especially the southern suburb. In the spring, the radish tastes very juicy and sweet. It is well-known that people in Nanjing like eating radish. And the people are even addressed as \'Nanjing big radish\', which means they are unsophisticated, passionate and conservative. From health perspective, eating radish can help to offset the stodgy food that people take during the Spring Festival".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[129]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_and_stadiums">Sports and stadiums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Sports and stadiums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nanjing_Olympic_Sports_Center_main_gym.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Nanjing_Olympic_Sports_Center_main_gym.jpg/200px-Nanjing_Olympic_Sports_Center_main_gym.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Nanjing_Olympic_Sports_Center_main_gym.jpg/300px-Nanjing_Olympic_Sports_Center_main_gym.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Nanjing_Olympic_Sports_Center_main_gym.jpg/400px-Nanjing_Olympic_Sports_Center_main_gym.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nanjing_Olympic_Sports_Center_main_gym.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nanjing Olympic Sports Center</div></div></div>\n<p>Nanjing\'s planned 20,000 seat Youth Olympic Sports Park Gymnasium will be one of the venues for the <a href="/wiki/2019_FIBA_Basketball_World_Cup" title="2019 FIBA Basketball World Cup">2019 FIBA Basketball World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[130]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As a major Chinese city, Nanjing is home to many professional sports teams. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jiangsu_Suning_FC" title="Jiangsu Suning FC">Jiangsu Suning FC</a>, the football club currently staying in <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Super_League" title="Chinese Super League">Chinese Super League</a>, is a long-term tenant of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanjing_Olympic_Sports_Center" title="Nanjing Olympic Sports Center">Nanjing Olympic Sports Center</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[131]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jiangsu_Dragons" title="Jiangsu Dragons">Jiangsu Nangang Basketball Club</a> is a competitive team which has long been one of the major clubs fighting for the title in China top level league, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Basketball_Association" title="Chinese Basketball Association">CBA</a>. Jiangsu Volleyball men and women teams are also traditionally considered as at top level in China volleyball league.\n</p><p>There are two major sports centers in Nanjing, <a href="/wiki/Wutaishan_Sports_Center" title="Wutaishan Sports Center">Wutaishan Sports Center</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanjing_Olympic_Sports_Center" title="Nanjing Olympic Sports Center">Nanjing Olympic Sports Center</a>. Both of these two are comprehensive sports centers, including stadium, gymnasium, natatorium, tennis court, etc. <a href="/wiki/Wutaishan_Sports_Center" title="Wutaishan Sports Center">Wutaishan Sports Center</a> was established in 1952 and it was one of the oldest and most advanced stadiums in early time of People\'s Republic of China.\n</p><p>Nanjing hosted the 10th National Games of PRC in 2005 and hosted the 2nd <a href="/wiki/2014_Summer_Youth_Olympics" title="2014 Summer Youth Olympics">summer Youth Olympic Games</a> in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[133]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2005, in order to host The 10th National Game of People\'s Republic of China, there was a new stadium, Nanjing Olympic Sports Center, constructed in Nanjing. Compared to <a href="/wiki/Wutaishan_Sports_Center" title="Wutaishan Sports Center">Wutaishan Sports Center</a>, which the major stadium\'s capacity is 18,500,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[134]</a></sup> Nanjing Olympic Sports Center has a more advanced stadium which is big enough to seat 60,000 spectators. Its gymnasium has capacity of 13,000, and natatorium of capacity 3,000.\n</p><p>On 10 February 2010, the 122nd <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IOC" title="IOC">IOC</a> session at Vancouver announced Nanjing as the host city for the 2nd Summer <a href="/wiki/Youth_Olympic_Games" title="Youth Olympic Games">Youth Olympic Games</a>. The slogan of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2014_Youth_Olympic_Games" title="2014 Youth Olympic Games">2014 Youth Olympic Games</a> was &#8220;Share the Games, Share our Dreams&#8221;. The Nanjing 2014 Youth Olympic Games featured all 28 sports on the Olympic programme and were held from 16 to 28 August. The Nanjing Youth Olympic Games Organising Committee (NYOGOC) worked together with the International Olympic Committee (IOC) to attract the best young athletes from around the world to compete at the highest level. Off the competition fields, an integrated culture and education programme focused on discussions about education, Olympic values, social challenges, and cultural diversity. The YOG aims to spread the Olympic spirit and encourage sports participation.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Nanjing is one of the most beautiful cities of mainland China with lush green parks, natural scenic lakes, small mountains, historical buildings and monuments, relics and much more, which attracts thousands of tourists every year.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buildings_and_monuments">Buildings and monuments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Buildings and monuments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Republic of China period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Because it was designated as the national capital, many structures were built around that time. Even today, some of them still remain which are open to tourists.\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen_Mausoleum" title="Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum">Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum</a> and its surrounding area</li>\n<li>Former <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Palace_(Nanjing)" title="Presidential Palace (Nanjing)">Presidential Palace, Nanjing</a> of ROC</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nationalist_government#Former_Sites" title="Nationalist government">Former Central Government of ROC Building Group along N. There are 75 institutions of higher learning till 2013. The number of National key laboratories, National key disciplines and the academicians of Chinese Academy of Sciences and Chinese Academy of Engineering all rank third in the nation. It boasts some of the most prominent educational institutions in the region, some of which are listed as follows:\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/Anhua_Gao" title="Anhua Gao">Anhua Gao</a>, Chinese-British author</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Jiangnan" title="Jiangnan">Jiangnan</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" of Nanjing">City Wall of Nanjing</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Walled_city_of_Nanjing" title="Walled city of Nanjing">Walled city of Nanjing</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ming_Palace" title="Ming href="/wiki/Nanjing_Salted_Duck" title="Nanjing Salted Duck">Nanjing Salted Duck</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanjing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Nanjingese, sometimes may be translated as Nanjinese, Nankinese, Nankingese, Nanjinger, Nankiner, etc.. In Nanjing dialect there is no difference between Nanjing and Nanjin or between Nanking and Nankin. This means the two pronunciations Jing and Jin in Mandarin Chinese pronounce the same in Nanjing dialect, and king and kin are also the same.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In <a href="/wiki/East_China" title="East China">East China</a>, in terms of urban population and urban area, the largest city is <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>, and the second largest is Nanjing.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-20">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Since becoming a southern capital, the city has been called Nanking (Nanjing, <span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#21335;&#20140;</span>) unofficially, and was officially named Nanjing (Nanking) after Peking (<a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> <span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#21271;&#20140;</span>, renamed from Peping or Beiping, <span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#21271;&#24179;</span>) became a capital city during the early <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a>; the name appears in Ming dynasty echo poem (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">&#34157;&#23376;&#39023; &#12298;&#22857;&#21644;&#26157;&#26126;&#22826;&#23376;&#37912;&#23665;&#35611;&#35299;&#35433;&#12299;&#65306;&#8220;&#23815;&#23997;&#22522;&#33290;&#23431;&#65292;&#30436;&#23994;&#36328;&#21335;&#20140;&#8221;</span>), for example. It\'s also unofficially called Nandu (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#21335;&#37117;</span>), and Nandu Fanhui Tu (<span lang="zh-Hant">&#12298;&#21335;&#37117;&#32321;&#26371;&#22294;&#12299;</span>; "Nandu Prosperity Picture") is an example.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-74"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-74">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Huai (Huai of Jianghuai <span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#27743;&#28142;</span>) is a big river north of Jiang (the river <a href="/wiki/Yangtze" title="Yangtze">Yangtze</a>), and the  Zhe (Zhe of Jiangzhe <span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#27743;&#27993;</span>)) is a big river south of Jiang.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-75"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-75">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The areas covered by such geographical names as Jiangnan, Dongnan and Xiajiang are not precisely defined. In ancient times the area was known as <a href="/wiki/Yang_Province" title="Yang Province">Yangchow</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">&#25562;&#24030;</span>). Sometimes the term Jianghai (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#27743;&#28023;</span>) is used because the region is where the Jiang (<a href="/wiki/Yangtze" title="Yangtze">Yangtze</a>, river) empties into the Hai (sea).</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-131"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-131">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Liuchao Gudu Bowuguan (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">&#20845;&#26397;&#21476;&#37117;&#21338;&#29289;&#39208;</span>)</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-132"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-132">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Jiangning Zhizao Bowuguan (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">&#27743;&#29999;&#32340;&#36896;&#21338;&#29289;&#39208;</span>)</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-133"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-133">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Nanjing Minsu Bowuguan (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">&#21335;&#20140;&#27665;&#20439;&#21338;&#29289;&#39208;</span>), located in Ganxi House (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#29976;&#29081;&#23429;&#31532;</span>) which is said to be the largest Chinese private house, with the nickname Ninety Nine And A Half Rooms.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-135"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-135">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A small museum and tomb honoring the 15th century seafaring admiral <a href="/wiki/Zheng_He" title="Zheng He">Zheng He</a> although his body was buried at sea off the <a href="/wiki/Malabar_Coast" title="Malabar Coast">Malabar Coast</a> near Calicut in western India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[126]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-136"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-136">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Jinling Shufa Silao Jinianguan (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">&#37329;&#38517;&#26360;&#27861;&#22235;&#32769;&#32000;&#24565;&#39208;&#65292;&#32993;&#23567;&#30707;&#12289;&#26519;&#25955;&#20043;&#12289;&#34157;&#23291;&#12289;&#39640;&#20108;&#36969;</span>)</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span At present, Taipei is the seat of the central government.)}}</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-21">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Nanjing is also called Jincheng (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#37329;&#22478;</span>, Gold City), derived from Jinling City. In addition, Jincheng was a city in Nanjing area. In the 1st year of Hsiankang in the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(265%E2%80%93420)" title="Jin dynasty (265&#8211;420)">Jin dynasty</a> (<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">AD</span></span><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>335), Langya (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#29807;&#29706;</span>), a prefectural governor <a href="/wiki/Huan_Wen" title="Huan Wen">Huan Wen</a> stationed in Jincheng, submitted a proposal to establish the prefecture of South Langya in the land of Jiangsheng (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#27743;&#20056;</span>) county, and then the city Jincheng became the capital city of the newly established South Langya Prefecture (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#21335;&#29807;&#29706;&#37089;</span>). The Jincheng later renamed Jinling township, in today\'s <a href="/wiki/Qinhuai_District" title="Qinhuai District">Qinhuai District</a>. (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">&#12298;&#33267;&#22823;&#37329;&#38517;&#26032;&#24535;&#12299;&#65306;&#8220;&#37329;&#22478;&#22312;&#22478;&#19996;&#20108;&#21313;&#20116;&#37324;&#65292;&#21556;&#31569;&#65292;&#20170;&#19978;&#20803;&#21439;&#37329;&#38517;&#20065;&#22320;&#21517;&#37329;&#22478;&#25101;&#21363;&#20854;&#22320;&#12290;&#8221; &#12298;&#33267;&#27491;&#37329;&#38517;&#26032;&#24535;&#12299;&#65306;&#8220;&#19978;&#20803;&#32291;&#37329;&#38517;&#37129;&#65292;&#33290;&#21517;&#37329;&#22478;&#25101;&#12290;&#26185;&#22826;&#20803;&#20843;&#24180;&#65292;&#35613;&#23433;&#21214;&#24107;&#20110;&#37329;&#22478;&#65292;&#21363;&#27492;&#12290;&#25110;&#31281;&#29701;&#37034;&#22478;&#12290;&#21688;&#24247;&#21021;&#65292;&#26707;&#28331;&#28858;&#29701;&#37034;&#20839;&#21490;&#65292;&#37806;&#37329;&#22478;&#12290;&#8221;</span>)</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">&#32593;&#26131;. <a class="external text"
